Without this, confidential or sensitive information could end up with the wrong access permissions, or personal data could be handled in the wrong way, increasing the risk of unauthorised disclosure, improper sharing, or keeping more personal information than allowed. To meet this requirement, the organisation must use its DoD security classification and access authorisation rules (Secret or Confidential) and its DoD privacy notice and data minimisation rules (aligned to HIPAA, GDPR, and CMMC) to dynamically apply the correct security and privacy labels to information system users and service accounts, to data stores such as files, databases, and message queues, and to the individuals represented in records (for example patients, employees, and contractors) and the personal data objects they relate to (such as HIPAA identifiers, GDPR personal data fields, and consent artefacts). The system should also keep these labels correct when access rights change, when data is reclassified, and when information is moved or aggregated, with evidence recorded in system audit logs.

#### Event-driven security/privacy label recalculation service

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT
Implement a central, policy-driven “attribute/label service” that dynamically associates and recalculates **security attributes** and **privacy attributes** for:
- **Subjects**: information system users and service accounts
- **Objects**: data objects (files, database records, message payloads)
- **Privacy subjects**: individuals represented in records
- **Privacy objects**: personal data objects (e.g., HIPAA/GDPR fields, consent artefacts)

The service must update attributes **as information is created and combined** (including aggregation/merge/move) and when relevant policy/context changes.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-16(1)** requires that the system **dynamically associate security and privacy attributes** with the organisation-defined subjects/objects **in accordance with** the organisation-defined security and privacy policies **as information is created and combined**.

This directly maps to the organisation-defined parameters:
- **ac-16.01_odp.01 / ac-16.01_odp.02** (security subjects/objects)
- **ac-16.01_odp.03 / ac-16.01_odp.04** (privacy subjects/personal data objects)
- **ac-16.01_odp.05 / ac-16.01_odp.06** (security and privacy policies)
- **ac-16.1_prm_1 / ac-16.1_prm_2** (organisation-defined subjects/objects and policies)

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Create a canonical attribute model** (security + privacy) used across the application and integrated data stores. Include fields for classification/access-control attributes and privacy/data-minimisation attributes.
2. **Encode the organisation-defined policies as policy-as-code** (versioned, testable). Implement:
   - **Security rules** for classification and access authorisation
   - **Privacy rules** for minimisation and privacy notice constraints
   - **Composition/aggregation rules** that define resulting attributes when information is **combined** (e.g., merged records, joined datasets, concatenated message payloads). Ensure the “resulting” label is computed from inputs rather than copied blindly.
3. **Implement event-driven recalculation** by subscribing to authoritative events from the system’s integration points:
   - IAM/IdP events for role/entitlement changes (to update security attributes for service accounts/users)
   - Data events for record create/update/delete and classification/security field changes (to update security attributes for data objects)
   - Data lineage/merge events for aggregation/combination (to recompute resulting object labels)
   - Privacy-context events when personal data fields/consent artefacts are created, linked, removed, or combined (to update privacy attributes for privacy subjects and personal data objects)
4. **Write-back and enforcement integration**: when labels change, propagate them to the relevant enforcement points (e.g., application authorisation checks, database row/field tagging, message routing/processing rules, and any data-handling controls). Ensure the application uses the service as the source of truth for label outcomes.
5. **Audit evidence**: for every recalculation, record machine-verifiable evidence including: triggering event, policy version, input attributes, computed resulting attributes, and affected subject/object identifiers. Retain logs according to enterprise logging/retention requirements.

## WHO (role responsible)
- **Solution owner / Application security architect**: defines attribute model and composition rules
- **Identity & access management engineer**: integrates IAM/IdP events and subject attribute updates
- **Data platform/integration engineer**: integrates data/merge events and write-back to data stores
- **Security engineering / compliance**: validates policy-as-code against AC-16(1) expectations and approves audit evidence format

## Acceptance criteria
- When a user/service account’s roles/entitlements change, the system updates the associated **security attributes** without manual intervention.
- When data is created, updated, moved, or **combined/aggregated**, the system recomputes and applies the correct **resulting security and privacy attributes** (no stale labels).
- Privacy attributes for individuals represented in records and for personal data objects are updated when personal data fields/consent artefacts are created, linked, removed, or combined.
- Every label change has audit evidence showing the triggering event, policy version, inputs, and computed outputs.
- The mechanism is demonstrably policy-driven (policy-as-code) and supports versioning and repeatable test cases.

**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Define a canonical security/privacy attribute schema for subjects and objects used by the application and integrated data stores
- [ ] Implement policy-as-code for the organisation-defined security classification/access rules and privacy/data-minimisation rules, including composition rules for combined information
- [ ] Integrate event subscriptions from IAM/IdP and from data creation/update/merge/move workflows to trigger label recalculation
- [ ] Build write-back mechanisms so computed labels are applied to the relevant enforcement points (authorisation checks, data tagging, and message handling)
- [ ] Implement audit logging for each recalculation (event, policy version, inputs, computed outputs, affected identifiers) and verify retention meets enterprise requirements
- [ ] Run end-to-end tests covering record aggregation/combination, role/entitlement changes, and privacy-context changes to confirm resulting labels are correct

### ac-16.2 — Attribute Value Changes by Authorized Individuals (Enhancement)

> **Overview**
>
> This expectation is about making sure that only the right people can change important access and privacy settings, and that every such change can be traced back to who did it and when. Without this, someone could quietly alter who is allowed to see information, or change how personal data is handled, leading to unauthorised access, privacy breaches, or incorrect decisions based on wrong settings. To meet this requirement, the organisation must keep an up-to-date list of named individuals (and any approved automated processes acting for them) who are allowed to set or change security-related and privacy-related attribute values. It must have clear, documented rules and procedures for how these changes are requested, approved, and carried out, configure the systems so unauthorised attempts are blocked, and ensure the system records each successful change in audit logs with the person (or approved process) responsible and the time of the change.

#### Authorised attribute-change workflow with auditable admin enforcement

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT
Implement a controlled capability for authorised individuals (and explicitly approved automated processes acting on their behalf) to define or change security and privacy attribute values, with enforcement that blocks unauthorised changes and with audit records for every successful change.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 AC-16(2) (Enhancement) requires that the organisation provides authorised individuals (or processes acting on behalf of individuals) the capability to define or change the value of associated security and privacy attributes, and that systems limit attribute creation/modification to authorised individuals. This directly supports preventing unauthorised access and privacy-impacting changes.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Create explicit authorisation for attribute writers**: In the enterprise IAM/IdP, define two privileged authorisation paths—one for **security attribute changes** and one for **privacy attribute changes**—mapped to named roles/groups (e.g., `Security-Attribute-Changers`, `Privacy-Attribute-Changers`).
2. **Require step-up authentication for attribute writes**: For any request that changes security/privacy attribute values, enforce re-authentication (phishing-resistant MFA where available) and block attribute writes from sessions that do not meet the step-up requirement.
3. **Route all attribute changes through an approved workflow**: Implement an admin portal/API endpoint that performs attribute changes only after a workflow step captures: requestor identity, target object, attribute name(s), proposed before/after values, justification, and an approver identity (ticket/workflow integration). The workflow must ensure only authorised individuals (or explicitly approved automation identities) can execute the change.
4. **Enforce enforcement at the application layer**: In the application, implement an authorisation check that permits attribute writes only when the caller’s identity is in the correct security/privacy changer role and the request is correlated to an approved workflow instance.
5. **Support “process acting on behalf of individuals” with explicit linkage**: For automated processes, use dedicated service identities that are only allowed to perform attribute changes when the request includes a verifiable linkage to the authorised individual’s approved workflow (e.g., workflow correlation ID signed/validated by the workflow service).
6. **Record audit evidence for every successful change**: Emit an audit event for each successful security/privacy attribute change including: actor identity (human or approved automation), timestamp, target object, attribute name, before/after values, and a correlation/request ID. Forward to SIEM and store with integrity protections (e.g., restricted write access / write-once or tamper-evident logging).
7. **Add detection for anomalous attribute changes**: Configure monitoring rules to alert on high-risk patterns (e.g., bulk changes, changes outside change windows, elevation of access-related attributes, changes by unusual admin identities).

## WHO (role responsible)
- **Application Security Engineer / IAM Engineer**: implement role mappings, step-up enforcement, and application-layer authorisation.
- **Application Owner / Privacy Officer (as applicable)**: define which attributes are security vs privacy and approve the workflow rules.
- **Security Operations (SOC) / SIEM Administrator**: configure audit forwarding, retention, and detection rules.
- **Change Management / Workflow Owner**: maintain the approved workflow and approver requirements.

## Acceptance criteria
- Only identities in the correct **security** or **privacy** changer authorisation path can successfully change the corresponding attribute values.
- Attribute write attempts by unauthorised identities are denied and do not result in attribute value changes.
- Every successful attribute change produces an audit record containing actor identity, timestamp, target object, attribute name, before/after values, and correlation/request ID.
- Automated processes can change attributes only when the request is tied to an approved workflow instance linked to an authorised individual.
- SIEM receives the audit events and detection rules generate alerts for configured high-risk attribute-change patterns.

**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Define and implement separate IAM roles/groups for security-attribute changers and privacy-attribute changers
- [ ] Implement step-up authentication (phishing-resistant MFA where feasible) for all security/privacy attribute write operations
- [ ] Create an admin portal/API that performs attribute changes only via an approved workflow with captured justification and approver identity
- [ ] Enforce application-layer authorisation checks that require both correct role membership and correlation to an approved workflow instance
- [ ] Configure automated attribute-change processes to use dedicated service identities and require verifiable linkage to an approved workflow correlation ID
- [ ] Implement tamper-evident audit logging for every successful attribute change (actor, timestamp, target, attribute, before/after, correlation ID) and forward to SIEM
- [ ] Add monitoring/detection rules for anomalous or high-risk security/privacy attribute changes and validate alerting in test

### ac-16.3 — Maintenance of Attribute Associations by System (Enhancement)

> **Overview**
>
> This expectation is about making sure the system always keeps the correct security and privacy labels attached to the right people and the right information, and that those label links cannot be quietly changed or corrupted. Without this, a person or automated process could be wrongly treated as allowed (or wrongly blocked), confidential or sensitive information could be shared or retained incorrectly, and required export or privacy handling could be bypassed without anyone noticing. To meet this, the organisation must clearly define which security and privacy labels matter (such as clearance, need-to-know, health and data-protection tags, and export-control handling), which users, service accounts, and privileged roles they apply to, and which datasets, files, and policy or configuration items they must be linked to. The organisation must also ensure the system uses these labels for automated decisions, and that any change to the label links or the underlying “known good” versions of key configuration and policy items is detected and flagged. Finally, it must document how labels are applied, how the system is built and configured to keep them correct, include this approach in security and privacy plans, assign responsibility to relevant staff and developers, and keep evidence that integrity checks and baseline comparisons are working.

#### Signed attribute assertions with integrity-checked bindings

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT
Implement an authoritative mechanism that maintains the association and integrity of the organisation-defined **security and privacy attributes** to the organisation-defined **subjects** and **objects**, and ensure automated policy decisions use only these maintained associations.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST AC-16(3) (enhancement) requires the system to **maintain the association and integrity** of the organisation-defined security/privacy attributes (param: **ac-16.3_prm_1**) to the organisation-defined subjects and objects (param: **ac-16.3_prm_2**). The guidance further expects that integrity of specific items (e.g., security configuration files) is maintained via integrity monitoring against **known-good baselines**, so that automated policy actions (access control decisions, information flow/disclosure decisions, retention expiry) remain reliable.

## HOW (specific approach)
1. **Define and version the attribute model**: create a controlled schema for the organisation-defined **security attributes** (ac-16.03_odp.01) and **privacy attributes** (ac-16.03_odp.02), and explicitly map which **subjects** (ac-16.03_odp.03/05) and **objects** (ac-16.03_odp.04/06) are eligible to carry which attributes.
2. **Issue tamper-evident, signed attribute assertions**: build or integrate an “attribute authority” service that issues **short-lived signed tokens** (e.g., JWT/JWS or equivalent) representing the maintained attribute associations for subjects and objects. Tokens must include:
   - attribute claims (security/privacy),
   - subject identifier and object identifier,
   - token issuance time and expiry,
   - a reference to the attribute model version.
3. **Bind object identifiers to integrity-monitored artefacts**: for objects such as **security configuration files / access-control policy objects** (ac-16.03_odp.04), compute and store a canonical identifier (e.g., hash of canonical metadata or content digest) and ensure the attribute authority only issues/refreshes bindings when the object’s current state matches the **known-good baseline** (integrity monitoring).
4. **Enforce using policy-as-code that consumes only maintained assertions**: implement ABAC/attribute-based enforcement at the application’s decision points (API gateway, service authorisation layer, data access layer). The enforcement component must:
   - validate the signature and expiry of attribute assertions,
   - deny by default if assertions are missing/invalid/out-of-date,
   - use the maintained security/privacy attributes to drive automated decisions (access control, information flow/disclosure, retention expiry).
5. **Detect and respond to association integrity anomalies**: integrate integrity monitoring alerts with the application’s authorisation decisioning so that when an object’s baseline integrity check fails or attribute bindings mismatch, the system raises an alert and restricts access/processing for affected subjects/objects.
6. **Operationalise evidence**: record (a) attribute model version, (b) assertion issuance/validation events, and (c) integrity monitoring results for the relevant objects to support auditability.

## WHO (roles responsible)
- **Security architect / IAM architect**: define attribute schema, subject/object mapping, and enforcement design.
- **Application security engineer / backend engineer**: implement attribute authority integration, policy-as-code enforcement, and denial-by-default behaviour.
- **Security operations (SOC) / security engineering**: configure integrity monitoring baselines for security configuration/policy objects and manage alert triage.
- **Data protection/privacy lead** (as applicable): validate privacy attribute definitions and mappings (e.g., HIPAA/GDPR tags).

## Acceptance criteria
- The application uses maintained, **signature-validated** attribute assertions for all automated access control, information flow/disclosure, and retention-expiry decisions involving the defined security/privacy attributes.
- For each defined object type (security configuration files/policy objects and privacy data stores/datasets/files), the system only accepts attribute bindings when integrity monitoring confirms the object matches the **known-good baseline** (or otherwise restricts/denies).
- If an attribute association is tampered with, or if an object’s integrity check fails, the system produces an auditable event and enforces **deny/restrict** for affected decisions.
- Evidence exists showing attribute model versioning, assertion validation outcomes, and integrity monitoring results for the relevant subjects/objects.


**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Define the controlled attribute schema for security attributes and privacy attributes and map each to eligible subjects and objects
- [ ] Implement or integrate an attribute authority that issues short-lived signed assertions binding ac-16.3_prm_1 to ac-16.3_prm_2
- [ ] Create canonical object identifiers for security configuration/policy objects and privacy data stores/datasets/files used in attribute bindings
- [ ] Configure integrity monitoring baselines for security configuration files and policy objects and enforce baseline match before issuing/refreshing bindings
- [ ] Implement policy-as-code enforcement that validates assertion signatures/expiry and denies by default when assertions are missing or invalid
- [ ] Integrate integrity anomaly detection with authorisation decisioning and alerting, and record audit evidence for assertion validation and integrity results

### ac-16.4 — Association of Attributes by Authorized Individuals (Enhancement)

> **Overview**
>
> This requirement is about making sure the right people can correctly tag information and accounts with the right protection level and privacy meaning, and that the system keeps those tags linked to the correct records. Without this, sensitive material could be mislabelled or left unlabelled, leading to unauthorised access, mishandling of regulated data, and confusion about who is allowed to see what. To meet this expectation, the organisation must define which security labels are allowed (PUBLIC, CONFIDENTIAL, SECRET, plus compartment codes) and which privacy tags are allowed (HIPAA role and GDPR role for people, and HIPAA PHI and GDPR personal data for information), and which users and service accounts are permitted to assign or change them. The system must let authorised people (or automated processes acting for them) apply these tags to the correct targets, including files, directories, and network ports in regulated use and on-prem document management items, while blocking invalid or inappropriate combinations. It must also guide privileged users with prompts or automated categorisation where chosen, check selections are valid, and record every change in an audit trail so the history can be traced.

#### Authorised attribute association with policy validation and audit trail

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT
Implement a capability that allows **authorised individuals (or authorised processes acting on their behalf)** to associate **organisation-defined security attributes** (e.g., PUBLIC/CONFIDENTIAL/SECRET + compartment codes) and **organisation-defined privacy attributes** (e.g., HIPAA/GDPR role tags for subjects; HIPAA PHI/GDPR personal data for objects) with **system-defined subjects and objects** (e.g., users/service accounts; files/directories/network ports; on-prem document management items).

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST AC-16(4) requires the system to provide the capability to associate **{{ac-16.4_prm_1}}** with **{{ac-16.4_prm_2}}** by **authorised individuals or processes acting on their behalf**, including support for prompting/automation and ensuring **valid attribute combinations**.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Create an authoritative attribute catalogue** in the application (or integrated governance service) defining:
   - Allowed **security labels**: PUBLIC, CONFIDENTIAL, SECRET, plus compartment codes.
   - Allowed **privacy tags** for **subjects** (HIPAA role, GDPR role) and for **objects** (HIPAA PHI, GDPR personal data).
   - Allowed **attribute combinations** and any required dependencies (e.g., SECRET requires at least one compartment code; privacy tags are only selectable for the correct target type).
2. **Implement eligibility and authorisation checks** for attribute association:
   - Define which **subjects** are eligible to be tagged (users/service accounts) and which **objects** are eligible (files/directories/network ports; document management items).
   - Enforce that only users in an **authorised assigners** group (or equivalent ABAC policy) can create/modify/remove associations.
   - Support “processes acting on behalf of individuals” by requiring service accounts to present an **auditable delegation context** (e.g., actor identity claim from the initiating user, or signed job metadata).
3. **Provide user prompting and/or automation with validation**:
   - For interactive flows, present controlled selection lists (drop-downs) for security labels and privacy tags.
   - Validate combinations server-side at the time of association (reject invalid selections; do not rely on client-side checks).
   - For automated categorisation, apply the same validation rules and only write associations when policy conditions and confidence thresholds are met.
4. **Ensure correct linking to the right records**:
   - Use authoritative identifiers for subjects and objects (e.g., immutable user/service-account IDs; file/directory inode/object IDs; network port identifiers; document management item IDs).
   - Store associations as first-class records tied to those identifiers so the correct subject/object relationship is preserved across updates.
5. **Generate auditable events for attribute association**:
   - Record who/what performed the association (actor identity, including delegated process context), what attributes were added/changed/removed, which subject/object identifiers were affected, and timestamps.
   - Forward audit events to the organisation SIEM/logging pipeline with fields suitable for later review.

## WHO (role responsible)
- **Application Security Engineer / Backend Engineer**: implement the attribute catalogue, eligibility/authorisation enforcement, validation logic, and audit event generation.
- **IAM/Identity Engineer**: configure the authorised assigners groups/roles and ensure service-account delegation context is available.
- **Data Protection Officer / Information Security Officer**: approve the allowed attributes, allowed combinations, and mapping of HIPAA/GDPR tags to subject/object types.

## Acceptance criteria
- Only members of the authorised assigners role (or authorised delegated processes) can associate or change security/privacy attributes for eligible subjects/objects.
- The system prevents invalid attribute combinations and enforces correct tag applicability by target type (subject vs object).
- Attribute associations are persisted against authoritative subject/object identifiers and remain correctly linked.
- Every association action (manual or automated) produces an audit record containing actor identity (or delegated actor context), affected subject/object identifiers, attributes changed, and timestamp, and these events are visible in the central logging/SIEM within the required retention window.

**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Define and implement an authoritative attribute catalogue for allowed security labels and privacy tags, including valid combinations by target type
- [ ] Implement server-side eligibility checks for eligible subjects and objects and enforce that only authorised assigners can create/modify/remove associations
- [ ] Add delegated-process support by requiring service-account actions to carry auditable actor context from the initiating authorised individual
- [ ] Implement interactive prompting (controlled selections) and automated categorisation that both call the same policy validation logic
- [ ] Persist attribute associations using authoritative immutable subject/object identifiers and verify correct linkage in integration tests
- [ ] Generate and forward audit events for attribute association changes (add/modify/remove) including actor/delegation context, affected identifiers, attributes changed, and timestamps

### ac-16.5 — Attribute Displays on Objects to Be Output (Enhancement)

> **Overview**
>
> This expectation is about making sure that whenever the system prints or shows a document on a screen, it clearly tells people what the information is, who it belongs to, and how it should be handled, without accidentally revealing sensitive details to the wrong person. Without this, someone could view or photograph a screen, or read a printed page, and learn full confidential or privacy-related information they are not entitled to see. To meet this, the organisation must ensure every output item includes the labels Classification, Handling Caveats, Data Owner, System/Network, Release/Distribution, and Privacy Notice ID, written in a way that a non-technical reader can understand. The system must show the full values for these attributes only when the viewer has unmasked access; otherwise it must show masked (redacted) values. The organisation must document the approach in clear procedures, ensure the system is built and configured to follow it, assign responsibility to the right staff, and keep records showing that the correct labels and masked-versus-full behaviour were used.

#### Attribute labels and full/masked values on all output renders

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT
Implement an output-rendering mechanism that, for every object the system transmits to output devices (printed pages, screens, PDFs, exports), displays the required **security and privacy attribute labels** in **human-readable form** and shows **full attribute values only when the subscriber has unmasked access**; otherwise it shows **masked/redacted values**.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST AC-16(5) enhancement requires that the system **“Display security and privacy attributes in human-readable form on each object that the system transmits to output devices”** using the organisation-defined **instructions** (ac-16.05_odp.01) and **naming conventions** (ac-16.05_odp.02). The guidance explicitly aims to mitigate risks such as **shoulder surfing** by ensuring full values are shown only when unmasked.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Create a canonical attribute display model** for the six required labels and map internal attribute data to human-readable strings:
   - Classification
   - Handling Caveats
   - Data Owner
   - System/Network
   - Release/Distribution
   - Privacy Notice ID
2. **Implement a single, central output-rendering component** (library/service) that all output channels call (web UI, mobile views, server-generated PDFs, report exports, print templates). This component must:
   - Always render the six labels on every output object.
   - Determine `display_mode` at render time based on the subscriber’s current authorisation context (unmasked vs masked).
   - Apply deterministic masking/redaction when `display_mode=masked`.
3. **Derive unmasked access from subscriber-aware authorisation** (e.g., session claims/entitlements from the enterprise IdP and/or application authorisation layer). Ensure the decision is made at **output-render time**, not only when data is stored.
4. **Prevent bypass** by enforcing that templates/handlers cannot render attribute sections without using the central renderer (e.g., code-level abstraction + CI/CD checks that fail builds if required label blocks are missing or if a template bypasses the renderer).
5. **Emit audit evidence per output object** from the renderer, capturing: output identifier, subscriber identity, attribute set/version, and `display_mode` (full|masked). This provides auditable proof that the correct behaviour occurred.
6. **Document the procedure** for granting unmasked access and for how masking is applied, including how developers must integrate the renderer into new output types.

## WHO
- **Application security engineer / platform engineer**: implement the central renderer, masking logic, and audit events.
- **Identity & access management (IAM) lead**: define/maintain the unmasked access entitlement used by the renderer.
- **Application developers**: integrate all output channels to call the renderer.
- **Compliance/audit owner**: validate evidence and approve the documented procedure.

## Acceptance criteria
- For every output object (screen, printed page, PDF/export), the six labels appear in human-readable form using the required naming conventions.
- When a subscriber does **not** have unmasked access, the output shows masked/redacted values (no full sensitive attribute values are visible).
- When a subscriber has unmasked access, the output shows full attribute values.
- CI/CD prevents new output templates from bypassing the renderer or omitting the required labels.
- Audit logs/events exist for outputs showing `display_mode=full|masked` and the attribute set/version used.

**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Define the canonical attribute display model and map internal attribute data to the required human-readable labels
- [ ] Implement a central output-rendering component that injects the six labels on every output object
- [ ] Implement subscriber-aware unmasked access evaluation and apply deterministic masking/redaction when unmasked access is not present
- [ ] Integrate all output channels (web, mobile, PDF/export, print templates) to call the central renderer
- [ ] Add CI/CD template linting to block any output path that bypasses the renderer or omits the required labels
- [ ] Emit per-output audit events including subscriber identity, attribute set/version, and display_mode (full|masked)
- [ ] Publish and maintain a procedure describing how unmasked access is granted and how masking is applied

### ac-16.6 — Maintenance of Attribute Association (Enhancement)

> **Overview**
>
> This requirement is about making sure the right people keep the right labels attached to the right users and data, and keep those labels accurate over time. In everyday terms, the organisation must correctly record which staff accounts and operational roles are allowed to do what, and which information and systems have which protection needs, as well as what personal information is involved, what it may be used for, and how long it must be kept. Without this, sensitive information could be accessed or handled incorrectly, and personal data could be processed or retained in ways that breach policy or law. To meet this expectation, the organisation must define clear rules for linking security and privacy labels to the correct people and data, assign responsibility to the appropriate information security and privacy staff (and system developers where needed), document the steps for doing it, and provide practical ways for staff to set and maintain these associations in line with the organisation’s attribute rules and privacy policies.

#### Attribute association maintenance via authoritative policy engine

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT
Implement an authoritative, automated mechanism that ensures personnel (and the system acting on their behalf) **associate and maintain** the organisation-defined **security and privacy attributes** with the organisation-defined **subjects and objects**, **in accordance with** the organisation-defined **security and privacy policies**.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-16(6)** enhancement requires: “Require personnel to associate and maintain the association of {{ac-16.6_prm_1}} with {{ac-16.6_prm_2}} in accordance with {{ac-16.6_prm_3}}.” Guidance clarifies that **individual users** (not just the system) must maintain attribute associations, but in practice this is satisfied by providing an authoritative process and mechanisms that personnel use to keep associations accurate over time.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
Create an **Attribute Policy Engine** that treats attribute associations as versioned, testable configuration and continuously reconciles them against authoritative sources.

1. **Define the attribute model and mapping rules** in the Attribute Management Standard (per {{ac-16.6_prm_1}} and {{ac-16.6_prm_2}}), including allowed values and validation constraints for:
   - Security attributes for subjects (e.g., data classification, system role, access authorisation level) and objects (e.g., data classification, handling caveats, encryption requirement).
   - Privacy attributes for subjects (e.g., personal data type, consent/processing basis) and objects (e.g., personal data category, retention/disclosure constraints).
2. **Implement an authoritative data ingestion layer** that normalises and maps inputs from enterprise systems into the attribute model, such as:
   - Identity provider / IAM role catalog (for subject identity and role).
   - HR system (for data subject representations).
   - Data catalog / metadata repository and asset inventory (for object classification and ownership).
   - OT tag registry / OT asset inventory (for OT data points, if applicable).
3. **Store attribute associations as versioned policy objects** (policy-as-code) that explicitly link:
   - Subject attributes ↔ subject identifiers (users, service accounts, OT operators).
   - Object attributes ↔ object identifiers (information assets, databases, OT data points).
4. **Drive enforcement and propagation** by integrating the policy engine with enforcement points used by the application ecosystem (e.g., conditional access/authorisation services and data access gateways), so that the maintained attribute associations are actually used to determine access and handling.
5. **Maintain associations over time** using reconciliation and drift detection:
   - Run scheduled and event-driven jobs that compare “expected attributes” (from authoritative sources + mapping rules) to “current attributes” (from IAM groups/entitlements and data metadata).
   - Automatically open remediation tickets when drift is detected.
   - Require **personnel approval** for exceptions and for cases where authoritative sources are missing/ambiguous (e.g., legacy OT tags), ensuring the “personnel maintain” aspect of AC-16(6) is met.
6. **Implement change control and audit evidence**:
   - Use version control for mapping rules and policy objects.
   - Record who approved exceptions, what changed, and why.
   - Provide periodic validation reports showing coverage and drift status.

## WHO
- **Information Security & Privacy Governance Lead**: owns the Attribute Management Standard and mapping rules ({{ac-16.6_prm_3}} alignment).
- **IAM/Data Governance Engineer**: implements the attribute policy engine, integrations, and reconciliation logic.
- **Application Owner / OT Operations Lead (where applicable)**: validates object classification/ownership inputs and approves exceptions.
- **Security Operations / Privacy Office (as applicable)**: reviews drift remediation outcomes and exception approvals.

## Acceptance criteria
- The organisation-defined security and privacy attributes are **mapped to the organisation-defined subjects and objects** according to the Attribute Management Standard and privacy policies.
- For each relevant subject/object type (users/service accounts/OT operators; information assets/databases/OT data points; HR/patient/consumer records), the system can demonstrate that the correct attribute associations are maintained after changes (e.g., role changes, data reclassification, consent updates).
- Drift detection identifies mismatches between expected and current attribute associations, and remediation tickets/approvals are recorded.
- Audit evidence exists for: mapping rule versions, policy object versions, exception approvals, and reconciliation/validation reports.

**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Define and publish the attribute schema and mapping rules in the Attribute Management Standard for both security and privacy attributes across the defined subject and object types
- [ ] Implement an attribute policy engine that stores attribute associations as versioned policy objects and validates them against allowed values and constraints
- [ ] Integrate the policy engine with authoritative sources (IdP/IAM, HR, data catalog/asset inventory, and OT tag registry where applicable) to normalise subject/object identifiers and attributes
- [ ] Configure enforcement/propagation so maintained attribute associations drive authorisation and data handling decisions in the application ecosystem
- [ ] Deploy reconciliation and drift detection jobs that compare expected vs current attribute associations and generate remediation workflows
- [ ] Establish an exception approval workflow for personnel to correct missing/ambiguous authoritative inputs and record approval evidence
- [ ] Produce periodic validation reports demonstrating attribute association coverage and drift status for audit readiness

### ac-16.7 — Consistent Attribute Interpretation (Enhancement)

> **Overview**
>
> This requirement is about making sure every part of your systems understands the same meaning when it receives information about who is allowed to access something and how data is allowed to move. If different components interpret these “rules of the road” differently, automated decisions could accidentally grant access that should be blocked or allow information to travel where it shouldn’t, creating real privacy and security failures. To meet this expectation, the organisation must clearly define, in writing, the exact meaning of every security and privacy attribute used across distributed components, for both access decisions and data-movement decisions, and publish a single organisation-approved guide so everyone follows the same interpretation. It must ensure all relevant components are configured to apply these rules, document how they are used in access and flow enforcement, assign named responsibility to appropriate staff and developers, keep evidence from configuration and audit records, include the approach in security planning and privacy policy, and verify through testing or review that components behave consistently.

#### Shared attribute semantics guide and policy-as-code enforcement

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT
Create and maintain a single, authoritative interpretation of all **security and privacy attributes** that are transmitted between distributed components, and ensure every component uses that same interpretation for **automated access enforcement** and **information-flow (flow) enforcement** decisions.

## WHY (control requirement)
AC-16(7) enhancement requires a **consistent interpretation** of security and privacy attributes transmitted between distributed system components so that access enforcement and flow enforcement actions are uniform and do not diverge due to different component assumptions.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Attribute inventory and classification**: Identify every security and privacy attribute used in automated access decisions and flow enforcement across the distributed system (e.g., API gateways, service-to-service calls, IAM/IdP claims, service mesh policies, application authorisation checks, data routing/egress controls). Record attribute name, source, transport mechanism, and where it is consumed.
2. **Define canonical semantics (single source of truth)**: For each attribute, define in writing (and in a machine-readable form) the canonical meaning, allowed values, data type, precedence rules, and edge-case handling (e.g., missing/unknown/empty values, conflicting attributes, default behaviour). Include explicit semantics for both:
   - **Access enforcement** (allow/deny/step-up/role mapping)
   - **Flow enforcement** (route/block/transform/egress restrictions)
3. **Publish an authoritative interpretation guide**: Release a versioned guide that is the organisation-approved reference for all teams and components. Also publish a versioned schema/contract (e.g., JSON schema + policy rule inputs) that components can validate against.
4. **Implement policy-as-code with shared artefacts**: Encode the interpretation guide into the enforcement layer(s) used by the system (e.g., central policy engine, gateway policy, service mesh policy, or shared authorisation library). Ensure all components reference the same versioned policy artefacts or shared interpretation library.
5. **Validate and fail closed on non-conformant attributes**: Add runtime validation so incoming attributes are checked against the contract; if attributes are missing/invalid/unknown, enforce the defined default semantics (preferably fail-closed for access/flow where feasible) and record the interpretation version used.
6. **Evidence and drift detection**: Log enforcement decisions with the received attribute values and the interpretation/policy version. Add CI/CD checks (contract tests and regression tests) to detect semantic drift between components and policy artefacts.

## WHO (role responsible)
- **Security architect / IAM & authorisation lead**: owns the canonical attribute semantics and interpretation guide.
- **Application security engineer / platform engineer**: implements policy-as-code integration and runtime validation.
- **Service owners / developers**: update components to consume the shared policy artefacts and remove bespoke/contradictory interpretations.
- **Compliance/GRC**: verifies audit evidence and that the guide is organisation-approved and version-controlled.

## Acceptance criteria
- There is a **single versioned interpretation guide** covering all security and privacy attributes used for access and flow enforcement.
- All distributed components consume the **same machine-readable contract/policy artefacts** (no component-specific semantic forks).
- Runtime behaviour is consistent: given the same attribute set, components produce the same access/flow decision according to the guide.
- Non-conformant attributes are handled according to defined semantics (documented and enforced), and enforcement logs include the **policy/interpretation version**.
- CI/CD includes automated contract/regression tests that fail when attribute semantics drift or enforcement logic diverges.

**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Inventory all security and privacy attributes used for automated access enforcement and flow enforcement across distributed components
- [ ] Define canonical attribute semantics (names, types, allowed values, precedence, and missing/unknown handling) for both access and flow decisions
- [ ] Publish a versioned, organisation-approved interpretation guide and a machine-readable attribute contract/schema
- [ ] Implement policy-as-code/shared interpretation artefacts in the enforcement points used by all components
- [ ] Add runtime validation to reject/quarantine non-conformant attributes and apply the defined fail-closed/default semantics
- [ ] Instrument enforcement logging to record received attribute values and the interpretation/policy version used
- [ ] Add CI/CD contract and regression tests to detect semantic drift between components and policy artefacts

### ac-16.8 — Association Techniques and Technologies (Enhancement)

> **Overview**
>
> This expectation is about making sure the labels that say how sensitive data is, and how it may be used, are securely tied to the data itself so they can’t be quietly changed. Without this, someone could tamper with those labels to gain access they should not have, or to route personal information through the wrong processing steps, undermining both privacy promises and access rules. To meet this, the organisation must use a defined method to cryptographically bind security and privacy labels to each piece of information by embedding signed label details in the data’s metadata, with the signing keys protected by hardware-based safeguards backed by a hardware root of trust. The system must check the signed security label every time access is requested, and check the signed privacy label every time the data is processed, and only then use the verified labels to make automated access and data-handling decisions. The organisation must document the approach, set up and record the required system behaviour, keep evidence in audit records, include it in both security and privacy plans, and assign clear responsibilities to information security and privacy staff and to system developers.

#### JWS-bound security/privacy labels verified at access & processing

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT
Implement the organisation-defined technique for **cryptographic binding of security/privacy labels to data using signed metadata (JWS) with keys protected by an HSM-backed hardware root of trust** (AC-16(8) prm_1). Embed **signed security labels** in object metadata and **signed privacy labels** in object metadata, then verify them at the required decision points.

## WHY (control requirement)
AC-16(8) enhancement requires implementing the organisation-defined **techniques and technologies** for associating security and privacy attributes to information. The guidance emphasises that binding can be achieved by **cryptographically binding attributes to information using digital signatures** and that verification must support automated access enforcement and flow enforcement.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Define the label-binding scheme**: create a canonical label schema for both security and privacy attributes (e.g., classification/handling and privacy processing constraints) and define how label claims are represented in JWS (including canonicalisation rules to prevent signature ambiguity).
2. **Implement JWS label envelopes**: build a label service/library that generates two JWS tokens per object: one for the **security label** and one for the **privacy label**. Embed each JWS in object metadata (or a sidecar metadata record that is cryptographically linked to the object identifier/hash, depending on the storage platform).
3. **Use HSM-backed keys**: configure signing keys in an HSM-backed KMS/HSM cluster with **non-exportable private keys** and ensure signing operations occur via the HSM interface. Record key identifiers/aliases used for each signature.
4. **Verify at access time (security)**: place an enforcement point in front of data access (e.g., API gateway/data access proxy/policy decision point) that extracts the security-label JWS from metadata, verifies the JWS signature and claim integrity, and only then evaluates authorisation decisions using the verified label values.
5. **Verify at processing time (privacy)**: place a processing/flow enforcement point (e.g., workflow/orchestration gateway, ETL/stream processing gateway, data-sharing/export service) that extracts and verifies the privacy-label JWS before allowing routing, transformation, analytics, export, or other processing steps.
6. **Fail safely**: if either JWS verification fails (signature invalid, key not trusted, claims malformed, or label missing), treat the corresponding label as **untrusted** and **deny/block** the relevant access or processing path. Ensure the system does not fall back to unauthenticated/unsigned labels.
7. **Produce audit evidence**: log verification outcomes (success/failure), key identifiers used, label values applied, and the decision point (access vs processing) to support auditability.

## WHO (roles responsible)
- **Security Architect / IAM & Data Governance Lead**: define label schema, canonicalisation, and enforcement decision logic.
- **Application Security Engineer / Platform Engineer**: implement label service/library, metadata embedding, and verification enforcement points.
- **HSM/KMS Administrator**: provision and manage HSM-backed signing keys and trust configuration.
- **Privacy Officer / Privacy Engineering**: validate privacy label semantics and processing-time enforcement requirements.

## Acceptance criteria
- For every protected object, the system embeds **signed security and privacy labels** as JWS in metadata using **HSM-protected signing keys**.
- At access time, the enforcement point verifies the **security-label JWS** and authorisation decisions are based only on verified label values.
- At processing time, the processing/flow enforcement point verifies the **privacy-label JWS** and processing/routing/export decisions are based only on verified label values.
- If verification fails or labels are missing/invalid, the system **denies or blocks** the relevant access/processing and records an audit event.
- Audit logs include verification status, key identifiers, and label values used at both decision points.

**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Define a canonical security-label and privacy-label schema and the JWS claim structure used for signing
- [ ] Implement a label-signing service that generates security-label JWS and privacy-label JWS and embeds them into object metadata
- [ ] Provision HSM-backed non-exportable signing keys and configure trust/verification parameters for the verification services
- [ ] Deploy an access-time enforcement point that verifies the security-label JWS before any authorisation decision is made
- [ ] Deploy a processing/flow enforcement point that verifies the privacy-label JWS before any processing, routing, or export occurs
- [ ] Configure fail-safe behaviour to deny/block when JWS verification fails or labels are missing/invalid
- [ ] Enable audit logging for verification outcomes, key identifiers, and label values used at both access and processing decision points

### ac-16.9 — Attribute Reassignment — Regrading Mechanisms (Enhancement)

> **Overview**
>
> This requirement is about making sure that any change to the security and privacy labels attached to information is done only through a trusted, approved re-labelling process. Without this, the organisation could accidentally or improperly treat sensitive information as less protected (or vice versa), leading to unauthorised access, incorrect handling, or privacy breaches. To meet this expectation, the organisation must use an approved data-labelling workflow that includes a formal policy-exception request, re-tagging carried out in a way that can be verified, and complete record-keeping of what changed and when. Before the process is used, it must be validated for security labels using automated checks against the approved exception and test examples, and validated for privacy labels by confirming the labels match the required format and by running tests that compare what different users can access before release. Only authorised staff and developers should carry out these reassignments, following documented procedures and keeping audit records.

#### Validated, ticketed label regrading service with signed retags

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT
Implement a single-purpose, trusted **Label Regrading Service** that is the only authorised mechanism for changing **security and privacy attributes** (labels) on information. The service must enforce **approved policy-exception ticketing**, perform **validated regrading** using the organisation-defined techniques, apply **cryptographic re-tagging**, and produce **audit evidence** linking each change to the exception and validation results.

## WHY (control requirement)
AC-16(9) requires that security and privacy attribute changes occur **only via regrading mechanisms validated using {{ insert: param, ac-16.9_prm_1 }}**. Because attribute changes can directly affect policy enforcement, the mechanism must operate consistently and correctly, and be tightly scoped (single purpose/limited function).

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Create the regrading mechanism as a dedicated service** (API/service component) that performs only label reassignment (no general data transformation). Restrict invocation so only the service can issue regraded label outputs.
2. **Govern every request with policy exception ticketing**: require an approved exception ticket ID (with scope and expiry) and bind it to the regrading request. Reject requests without a valid, approved ticket reference.
3. **Security attribute validation (pre-release)**: before releasing any regraded label, run automated rule checks against the approved policy exception and execute the organisation-defined **security test vectors** (golden datasets/edge cases) to confirm the regrading rules behave as intended.
4. **Privacy attribute validation (pre-release)**: validate privacy labels using **schema conformance checks** and run **differential access-control tests** comparing access outcomes before vs after regrading, ensuring the privacy attribute change does not violate expected access-control behaviour.
5. **Cryptographic re-tagging**: generate integrity-protected, verifiable label tokens for the regraded attributes (e.g., signed tokens) that include at minimum: exception ID, label version, and a hash/evidence reference to the validation run.
6. **Immutable audit logging**: write append-only audit records (and forward to SIEM) capturing who/what/when/why, the exception ticket ID, input label state, output label state, and validation results (including run identifiers and pass/fail outcomes). Ensure audit records are tamper-evident (e.g., WORM/object lock).
7. **Operational controls**: document the service runbook and validation procedures; restrict administrative access to the service; ensure the service is deployed with separate environments (dev/test/prod) and that only the validated production configuration can be used.

## WHO (role responsible)
- **Application/Data Owner / Information Security Officer**: approves the label taxonomy, policy exception workflow requirements, and validation acceptance criteria.
- **Platform/Software Engineering Lead**: implements the Label Regrading Service, cryptographic signing, and API restrictions.
- **Security Engineering / GRC**: defines and maintains the validation techniques (test vectors, schema rules, differential access test methodology) and verifies audit evidence.
- **Operations / SOC**: ensures immutable log retention, SIEM forwarding, and monitoring/alerting on regrading activity.

## Acceptance criteria
- The only path to security/privacy label reassignment is the Label Regrading Service; direct label changes are technically blocked or strongly controlled.
- Every regrading operation requires an approved policy exception ticket reference and fails closed if missing/invalid/expired.
- Security regrading is validated using automated rule checks against the approved exception and the configured security test vectors before any regraded label is released.
- Privacy regrading is validated using schema conformance checks and differential access-control tests before any regraded label is released.
- Regraded labels are cryptographically re-tagged (integrity-protected) and include verifiable linkage to the exception ID and validation evidence.
- Audit logs are complete, immutable/tamper-evident, and include ticket ID, actor identity, timestamps, input/output labels, and validation results.
- Evidence is reproducible for auditors (validation run IDs and audit log entries can be correlated end-to-end.

**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Implement a dedicated, single-purpose Label Regrading Service that is the only component allowed to output regraded security/privacy labels
- [ ] Integrate the service with policy exception ticketing and enforce mandatory, valid, in-scope exception ticket IDs with expiry checks
- [ ] Configure automated security validation using rule checks against the approved exception and execute the approved security test vectors before releasing any regraded label
- [ ] Configure privacy validation using schema conformance checks and differential access-control tests (before/after) before releasing any regraded label
- [ ] Add cryptographic re-tagging for regraded labels, embedding exception ID and validation evidence references in the signed token
- [ ] Enable immutable, append-only audit logging for each regrading request (actor, timestamps, input/output labels, ticket ID, validation run IDs and results) and forward to SIEM
- [ ] Restrict administrative access to the service and document the runbook and validation procedures for production operation and audit evidence

### ac-16.10 — Attribute Configuration by Authorized Individuals (Enhancement)

> **Overview**
>
> This requirement is about making sure only the right people can decide what labels and rules the system uses to describe who should be allowed to access information and how that information should be handled. If unauthorised staff could create or change these labels and values, they could accidentally or deliberately give themselves or others access they should not have, or misclassify sensitive information, creating real compliance and privacy failures. To meet this expectation, the organisation must provide authorised individuals with the ability to define or change the types and values of both access-related (security) and privacy-related attributes that can be linked to people and to information. It must also have clear written procedures and documented rules stating who is authorised, ensure the system settings enforce those permissions, and keep records of changes so any attempt to alter attributes can be traced to the person who made it.

#### Authorised-only security/privacy attribute schema configuration

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT
Implement a controlled, auditable capability for authorised individuals to define or change the **type and value** of security and privacy attributes that can be associated with **subjects and objects**.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-16(10)** requires that the system limits the ability to create or modify the **type and value** of security and privacy attributes available for association with subjects and objects to **authorised individuals only**. Because attribute content can directly affect access decisions, the enforcement must be technical (not only procedural) and changes must be traceable.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Create dedicated admin roles and enforce them technically**: Define separate authorisation roles for security-attribute schema management and privacy-attribute schema management (e.g., `AttributeSchemaAdmin(Security)` and `AttributeSchemaAdmin(Privacy)`). Map these roles to individuals via the enterprise IdP (SSO) and enforce them at both the **UI** and **API/backend** layers for all schema operations (create/update/delete attribute types and values).
2. **Require phishing-resistant MFA and hardened admin sessions**: For any attribute-schema configuration action, require phishing-resistant MFA (e.g., FIDO2/passkeys) and apply conditional access (device posture/risk-based sign-in) for admin consoles.
3. **Treat attribute schemas as versioned configuration with controlled deployment**: Store attribute schema definitions as versioned configuration (e.g., in a controlled repository). Apply automated validation (policy-as-code or schema validation) before changes can be deployed.
4. **Block unauthorised or out-of-policy changes**: Ensure the application rejects any request to associate subjects/objects using attribute types/values that are not currently deployed/approved. Enforce allow-lists server-side so unauthorised users cannot introduce new attribute types/values.
5. **Implement an approval workflow for schema changes**: Require a documented approval step (ticket/workflow) plus automated checks; prevent direct production edits by default (only allow deployment of approved versions).
6. **Generate audit evidence for every change**: Emit audit events for each schema change capturing: initiating identity, timestamp, attribute type/value changed, old vs new values, target environment (dev/test/prod), approval/ticket reference, and whether the action was allowed or denied. Forward to SIEM and retain per organisational logging retention.

## WHO (role responsible)
- **Application Security Engineer / IAM Engineer**: implement role mappings, API enforcement, and audit event instrumentation.
- **Application Owner / Data Governance Lead**: define which individuals are authorised for security vs privacy attribute schema changes and approve the workflow.
- **Privileged Access Administrator**: manage admin role assignments and periodic access reviews.

## Acceptance criteria
- Only users in the authorised roles can create/update/delete security and privacy attribute types/values; attempts by other users are technically denied.
- Admin schema changes require phishing-resistant MFA and occur only within hardened admin sessions.
- The system rejects associations using attribute types/values not present in the approved/deployed schema set.
- Every schema change produces an auditable record containing who/what/when/old/new and approval reference, and these events are visible in SIEM.
- Production schema changes are deployed only from approved, validated versions (no direct hot edits).

**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Define and document separate authorised roles for security-attribute and privacy-attribute schema management, and map them in the enterprise IdP
- [ ] Implement server-side authorisation checks on all attribute-schema configuration endpoints (UI and API) to permit only those roles
- [ ] Enforce phishing-resistant MFA and conditional access for attribute-schema configuration sessions
- [ ] Store attribute schema definitions as versioned, validated configuration and require deployment only from approved versions
- [ ] Add server-side allow-list enforcement so subject/object associations can only use deployed/approved attribute types and values
- [ ] Instrument and forward audit events for every schema change (who/when/what/old/new/approval reference) and verify SIEM ingestion
- [ ] Run a test proving unauthorised users cannot create/modify attribute types/values and cannot associate subjects/objects using unapproved attributes

### ac-17 — Remote Access (Control)

> **Overview**
>
> This requirement is about making sure only approved ways of connecting from outside the organisation are allowed to reach your systems, and that every such connection is set up and used in a controlled, documented way. Without clear rules and prior approval, staff or devices could connect using the wrong method, bypass safeguards, or gain access before anyone has checked that the connection is safe and appropriate, increasing the risk of unauthorised access and data loss. To meet this expectation, the organisation must list every type of remote access it permits (such as dial-up, broadband, or wireless), and for each type it must write down plain-language rules on who may use it and what is allowed or prohibited, the exact connection and configuration requirements, and practical guidance for how to implement it correctly. The organisation must also ensure that each remote access type is formally approved before any connections are allowed, and that it can produce records showing remote access activity for review.

#### Remote access types registry with pre-authorisation enforcement

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT
Create and operate an organisation-controlled registry of every **remote access type** permitted to reach the application/system (e.g., encrypted VPN, ZTNA, vendor support via approved jump host). For each type, define **who may use it**, **usage restrictions**, **required connection/configuration settings**, and **implementation guidance**. Ensure each remote access type is **formally authorised before any connections are allowed**, and that remote access activity is auditable.

## WHY (control requirement)
AC-17 requires that remote access is controlled by explicitly defining allowed remote access types and ensuring each type is **authorised prior to allowing remote access**. Guidance also notes that encrypted VPNs can provide confidentiality/integrity assurance, but remote access still traverses external networks and may affect monitoring/availability—so enforcement must be explicit and auditable.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Build a Remote Access Types Register** for the application/system and each environment (prod/test/DR). Each entry must include: remote access type name, allowed user groups/roles, permitted source networks/endpoints, required authentication method(s), required encryption/tunnel profile (where applicable), allowed protocols/ports, and explicit prohibited behaviours (e.g., split tunnelling unless explicitly approved).
2. For each remote access type, attach controlled documents:
   - **Remote Access Usage Restrictions** (who/when/where/what is prohibited)
   - **Connection/Configuration Requirements** (gateway/client/server settings, crypto/auth requirements, routing constraints)
   - **Implementation Runbook** (step-by-step setup and verification checklist)
3. **Enforce authorisation at the access entry point** (VPN concentrator / ZTNA gateway / bastion/jump host) and at identity layer:
   - Only allow gateway profiles/policies that correspond to an **approved** registry entry.
   - Use identity conditional access (or equivalent) to require the user/device/session to match the authorised remote access type and posture.
4. Implement an **authorisation workflow gate** so that enabling a remote access type requires prior approval (e.g., security + system owner). The workflow must prevent deployment/enabling of gateway/identity policies until the registry entry is approved.
5. **Generate audit evidence** by ensuring logs capture: user identity, remote access type, connection start/stop time, source endpoint/network, and the gateway policy/profile used. Link authorisation records to the corresponding gateway/IdP events.
6. Add **drift detection**: periodically validate that enabled gateway/identity policies match the approved registry entries; alert on any deviations.

## WHO
- **Application/System Owner**: accountable for defining permitted remote access types and approving usage restrictions.
- **Security Engineering / IAM Team**: implements enforcement at gateway/IdP and maintains the registry templates/runbooks.
- **Infrastructure/Network Team**: implements and validates gateway configuration changes via the approved workflow.
- **Audit/Compliance or GRC**: reviews evidence and ensures authorisation records are complete and retained.

## Acceptance criteria
- The Remote Access Types Register exists and is complete for the application/system environments.
- For every permitted remote access type, there is an approved authorisation record dated **before** any enabling/connection activity.
- Gateway/IdP enforcement prevents unauthorised remote access types from being used (attempts fail or are blocked).
- Audit logs show remote access activity with remote access type, user identity, timestamps, and source endpoint/network.
- Drift checks confirm enabled policies match the approved registry entries, with documented remediation for any mismatch.

**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Create a Remote Access Types Register covering all permitted remote access methods for each application environment
- [ ] Define and document usage restrictions, connection/configuration requirements, and implementation runbooks per remote access type
- [ ] Implement gateway/IdP enforcement so only approved remote access type profiles/policies can be used
- [ ] Establish an authorisation workflow gate that requires approval before enabling any remote access type
- [ ] Configure audit logging to record remote access type, user identity, timestamps, and source endpoint/network
- [ ] Run periodic drift detection to verify enabled remote access policies match the approved registry and remediate mismatches

### ac-17.1 — Monitoring and Control (Enhancement)

> **Overview**
>
> This requirement is about making sure every time someone connects to your systems from a distance, the organisation automatically checks that it is allowed and records what happened. Without this, unauthorised people could try to break in, or staff could connect in ways that violate company rules, and you might only discover it after damage has been done. To meet this expectation, the organisation must use automated tools to continuously monitor remote connections from all supported device types, including servers, laptops, workstations, smartphones and tablets, and to automatically enforce the organisation’s remote access rules by allowing or blocking sessions based on those rules. It must also automatically produce clear records of both monitoring activity and any allowed or blocked outcomes, using the agreed details so that later reviews can prove compliance. The organisation should be able to show that these monitoring and blocking features are switched on in current settings, work in practice, and are reviewed by the responsible people.

#### Policy-enforced remote access with automated monitoring and audit

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT
Implement automated mechanisms that (1) continuously monitor remote access methods and (2) automatically control/enforce remote access sessions (allow/deny/restrict) at connection/session establishment time.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST AC-17(1) enhancement requires the organisation to “employ automated mechanisms to monitor and control remote access methods”. The guidance notes that monitoring and control should audit remote user connection activities across system components and that audit logging for remote access is enforced by AU-2, with event details defined in AU-2(a).

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Centralise remote access entry points** so all remote access methods (e.g., VPN, RDP/SSH jump hosts, remote access portals, ZTNA apps, secure web access) route through a **policy-enforcing gateway** (e.g., ZTNA/secure access proxy or VPN with policy enforcement) integrated with the organisation’s **central identity provider (IdP)**.
2. **Define remote access policy rules** in the IdP/gateway for automated enforcement, including at minimum: allowed user groups/roles, required authentication strength (e.g., phishing-resistant MFA where feasible), device posture/compliance requirements, and any network/location constraints.
3. **Enforce allow/deny at session establishment**: configure the gateway/IdP so that remote sessions are created only when policy evaluation succeeds; otherwise sessions are blocked/denied automatically.
4. **Continuously monitor remote access sessions** by enabling telemetry from the enforcement points (IdP/gateway) for every remote access attempt and session lifecycle event (attempt, success, denial, session start/stop where available).
5. **Generate auditable evidence for both monitoring and control outcomes** by emitting structured remote-access audit events from the enforcement points into the organisation’s logging pipeline/SIEM, ensuring the event fields align with the organisation’s AU-2 remote-access audit event definitions (method, user, target system/service, source device/IP where available, and outcome).
6. **Operationalise detections and response hooks**: create automated alerts for high-risk patterns (e.g., repeated denied attempts, anomalous device posture, access to sensitive targets) and route to the existing incident/response workflow (SOAR/ticketing) to support timely investigation.

## WHO (role responsible)
- **Security architect / IAM engineer**: designs the policy model and enforcement points.
- **Network/security engineering**: implements gateway/ZTNA/VPN policy enforcement and routing.
- **SIEM/logging engineer**: maps and validates remote-access audit event fields to AU-2/AU-2(a) requirements.
- **SOC/incident response lead**: validates alerting, triage, and escalation paths.

## Acceptance criteria
- Every configured remote access method in scope is routed through the policy-enforcing gateway/IdP (no bypass paths).
- For remote access attempts, the system automatically evaluates policy and **allows or denies** sessions without manual intervention.
- For each attempt and outcome, the enforcement points produce **audit events** that are ingested into the SIEM and contain the required remote-access audit details per the organisation’s AU-2/AU-2(a) definitions.
- Demonstrated test results show: (a) compliant devices/users can establish sessions; (b) non-compliant or unauthorised users are denied; (c) both outcomes are visible in SIEM with correct fields and timestamps.
- Monitoring/alerting is enabled and produces actionable alerts for defined high-risk scenarios (at least denied-attempt spikes and anomalous posture).

**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Inventory all in-scope remote access methods and identify enforcement points to eliminate bypass paths
- [ ] Integrate each remote access entry point with the central IdP and configure required authentication strength and authorisation groups/roles
- [ ] Implement policy-enforced session establishment at the gateway/IdP (allow/deny/restrict) based on device posture and remote access rules
- [ ] Enable continuous telemetry from the enforcement points for remote access attempts and session lifecycle events
- [ ] Configure SIEM ingestion and validate that remote-access audit events match the organisation’s AU-2/AU-2(a) remote-access event schema
- [ ] Create and test automated detections for denied-attempt anomalies and access to sensitive targets, with routing to SOC workflows

### ac-17.2 — Protection of Confidentiality and Integrity Using Encryption (Enhancement)

> **Overview**
>
> This requirement is about making sure that when people connect to your systems from elsewhere, the information they send and receive is kept secret and cannot be tampered with while it travels over the internet. Without this, an attacker could intercept remote connections, read sensitive data, or alter what gets sent, potentially leading to fraud, data leaks, or unauthorised changes. To meet this expectation, the organisation must use approved, secure encryption for every remote access session, using a recognised secure remote method such as a private network connection and/or secure web connection, and ensure it is correctly set up. It must document which encryption methods are used and how they are configured, keep the relevant records and audit information showing encryption was active, and make sure remote-access instructions and staff procedures follow the organisation’s access rules. The organisation should also maintain design and security planning documents that clearly explain how encryption protects remote access.

#### Enforce VPN/TLS for all remote access with auditable crypto settings

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT
Implement cryptographic mechanisms so that **every remote access session** to the application environment is protected for **confidentiality and integrity** using approved encryption (e.g., **VPN** and/or **TLS**), with configurations that prevent any unencrypted or weakly encrypted remote path.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST AC-17(2) enhancement requires: **“Implement cryptographic mechanisms to protect the confidentiality and integrity of remote access sessions.”** Guidance notes that **VPN** and **TLS** are examples that provide end-to-end communications security.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Standardise approved remote access paths**: Define in the access control policy that remote access to the application environment is only permitted via approved encrypted mechanisms (e.g., **VPN tunnel** for internal network access and/or **TLS** for any remote web/API administration portals).
2. **Enforce encryption at the network edge**: Configure firewalls/security groups/ingress rules so that internal resources are not reachable directly from the internet; only allow traffic that terminates on the approved VPN concentrator or approved TLS endpoints. Block or redirect any attempt to bypass these paths.
3. **Configure strong, approved cryptography**: Apply organisation-approved cryptographic baselines to VPN and TLS endpoints (protocol versions, cipher suites, key exchange, certificate validation, and session renegotiation/termination behaviour). Disable legacy/insecure options.
