- **Security Operations (SOC) / Compliance Monitoring:** monitors encryption compliance and reviews audit evidence.
- **System Owner / Authorising Official (or delegated governance role):** approves encryption scope and policy changes.

## Acceptance criteria
- For **100% of DoD-managed mobile devices/endpoints**, the MDM/MAM reports the **container encryption policy as applied and active** for the defined encrypted scope.
- The encrypted scope is **documented** (which data containers/structures are encrypted) and matches the deployed MDM/MAM policy.
- Audit logs in the SIEM show **encryption enablement status** and **encryption policy/configuration changes** with timestamps and affected device/app identifiers.
- Attempts to access encrypted container data via unmanaged paths are **blocked or controlled** according to the configured MDM/MAM restrictions.
- Encryption policy configuration is **versioned**, change-approved, and traceable to the system security documentation.


**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Identify and document the exact managed-app data containers/structures to be container-encrypted on DoD-managed mobile devices
- [ ] Configure MDM/MAM policies to enforce container-based encryption for the defined scope (confidentiality and integrity)
- [ ] Enforce device compliance prerequisites (strong unlock and security posture) as conditions for container encryption to remain active
- [ ] Restrict plaintext export/copy/share paths for encrypted containers using MDM/MAM controls where supported
- [ ] Enable MDM/MAM audit logging and forward encryption-policy and encryption-status events to the SIEM with sufficient retention
- [ ] Version-control the encryption policy configuration baseline and require change approval for any encryption-related updates
- [ ] Assign named roles for encryption policy administration, compliance monitoring, and approval of encryption scope changes

### ac-20 — Use of External Systems (Control)

> **Overview**
>
> This requirement is about making sure that when people use outside systems to reach the organisation’s services or handle organisation information, it is done safely and under clear, agreed rules. Without this, sensitive information could be exposed, altered, or lost because outside providers or devices may not protect data in the same way, and problems might not be spotted or reported quickly. The organisation must only permit access from external systems when the access and data-handling rules match the trust agreements it has with the owners of those external systems, and those agreements must be written and cover which applications can be used, the maximum information level allowed (up to Secret maximum), the access rules, required activity recording, and how incidents are reported within 24 hours. For any permitted external-system use, the external systems must enforce strong protections such as encryption while data moves and when stored, requiring a second factor to log in, keeping audit records, and managing weaknesses. The organisation must also prohibit personally owned devices, unmanaged contractor-managed systems, and public cloud services unless an approved authorisation boundary is in place.

#### External system trust agreements with enforceable access limits

- **Category:** Manual
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT
Implement a standard, written “external system trust agreement” (terms and conditions) for every external system used to access organisational systems, and enforce those terms through technical access controls (application allow-lists, identity/MFA, encryption, audit logging, and vulnerability/patch expectations). Explicitly prohibit the defined external system types (e.g., personally owned devices, unmanaged contractor-managed systems, and unauthorised public cloud).

## WHY (control requirement)
AC-20 requires that external systems are used only under specific terms and conditions that, at a minimum, address:
- the **types of applications** that can be accessed from external systems;
- the **highest security category of information** that can be processed, stored, or transmitted on external systems (per organisation parameter: **Secret max**);
- and that the organisation establishes terms consistent with trust relationships, including **controls asserted** on the external systems (e.g., encryption in transit/at rest, MFA, audit logging, vulnerability management, and incident notification).
It also allows the organisation to **prohibit** specified types of external systems.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. Create an “External System Trust Pack” template that includes (at minimum) the required **terms and conditions** and the **controls asserted** annex, aligned to the organisation-defined parameters:
   - Allowed applications (application allow-list per external system type)
   - Data classification ceiling: **Secret max**
   - Access rules (who can access, from where, and under what conditions)
   - Logging requirements (audit logging)
   - Incident/breach notification requirement: **within 24 hours**
   - Security control assertions: **encryption in transit and at rest**, **MFA**, **audit logging**, **vulnerability management**, **incident notification within 24 hours**
2. Maintain a registry of all external systems and external system types permitted to access organisational systems, and require a signed trust agreement for each entry (or a documented rationale where a trust relationship is already established by law/directive/policy).
3. Enforce the trust terms technically using the enterprise access stack:
   - Use an identity provider with conditional access to require **phishing-resistant MFA** for authorised individuals.
   - Enforce **application allow-lists** via ZTNA/secure access gateways, API gateways, or reverse proxies so only approved applications are reachable.
   - Enforce **encryption in transit and at rest** for any permitted data flows/storage on the external system side (contractual requirement plus technical validation where feasible).
   - Enable and forward **audit logs** from the access path and the external integration endpoints to the SIEM.
4. Implement explicit deny controls for prohibited external system types:
   - Block personally owned devices.
   - Block unmanaged contractor-managed systems.
   - Block public cloud services unless an approved authorisation boundary exists.
   (Enforcement should be done via device posture checks, network access policies, and cloud authorisation/boundary controls.)
5. Add operational verification:
   - Require evidence of vulnerability management and patching for permitted external systems (e.g., scan reports or attestations) at an agreed cadence.
   - Validate that incident/breach notification within **24 hours** is contractually required and that the external party has an identified incident contact and escalation path.

## WHO (role responsible)
- **Information Security / CISO office**: owns the trust agreement template, prohibition list, and governance.
- **Service Owner / Application Owner**: ensures the correct application allow-list and data classification ceiling are specified per external system.
- **Identity & Access Management (IAM) team**: implements MFA/conditional access and access enforcement.
- **Network/Security Engineering**: implements ZTNA/secure access and logging integration.
- **Procurement/Legal**: ensures trust agreements are signed and enforceable.
- **Third-party/vendor management**: maintains the external system registry and evidence collection.

## Acceptance criteria
- For every permitted external system, there is a **signed written trust agreement/terms and conditions** covering allowed applications, **Secret max** data limits, access rules, audit logging, and **incident notification within 24 hours**.
- Technical enforcement exists such that only **approved applications** are accessible from external systems and **MFA** is required for authorised individuals.
- Encryption in transit and at rest is asserted in the trust terms and is technically validated where feasible.
- Audit logs for external access are generated and forwarded to the SIEM.
- Prohibited external system types are blocked by policy and technical controls (no access path exists for personally owned devices, unmanaged contractor-managed systems, or unauthorised public cloud).
- Evidence of vulnerability management/patching and an incident escalation contact are on file for each permitted external system.

**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Create an External System Trust Pack template covering allowed applications, Secret max data limits, access rules, audit logging, and 24-hour incident notification
- [ ] Define and publish prohibited external system types and the enforcement expectations for each (personally owned devices, unmanaged contractor-managed systems, unauthorised public cloud)
- [ ] Establish and maintain an external system registry requiring a signed trust agreement (or documented trust rationale) for every permitted external system
- [ ] Implement IAM conditional access requiring phishing-resistant MFA for authorised individuals accessing via external systems
- [ ] Enforce application allow-lists using ZTNA/secure access or API gateway controls so only approved applications are reachable
- [ ] Configure audit logging for external access paths and forward logs to the SIEM for monitoring and evidence
- [ ] Require and retain evidence of vulnerability management/patching and validate incident escalation contacts for each permitted external system

### ac-20.1 — Limits on Authorized Use (Enhancement)

> **Overview**
>
> This requirement is about making sure that when staff use an outside service to reach your systems or handle your information, it is only allowed when the outside provider has been properly checked or formally agreed. Without this, an outside platform could be weak on protection or privacy, letting sensitive information leak, be altered, or be used in ways your organisation never intended, which could lead to financial loss, legal trouble, and reputational damage. To meet this expectation, the organisation must permit only authorised people to use external systems for accessing, processing, storing, or sending organisation-controlled information after either verifying that the external system has the right security and privacy protections in place (as described in the organisation’s own policies and plans), or keeping an approved written agreement with the organisation that hosts the external system. The organisation must also keep the relevant proof or approved agreement on file so it can be shown when access is granted.

#### Assurance-gated external system access for authorised users

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT
Implement an assurance gate so that authorised individuals can only access, or use external systems to process, store, or transmit organisation-controlled information when the external system has either (1) been verified to have the required security/privacy controls, or (2) an approved written agreement is retained for that external system.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-20(1) Limits on Authorized Use (Enhancement)** requires that external-system use by authorised individuals is permitted **only after** the organisation has verified the external system’s required controls (e.g., via independent assessments/attestations) **or** retained an **approved** connection/processing agreement.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Create and maintain an External System Register** covering each external system/vendor used for access or for processing/storing/transmitting organisation-controlled information (including purpose, information types, data flows, user populations, and environment).
2. **Define an External System Assurance Checklist** mapped to your organisation’s security/privacy policies and plans (e.g., identity/authentication expectations, encryption in transit/at rest, logging/audit capability, data handling/retention, breach notification, subprocessors, and privacy controls). Ensure the checklist is risk-tier aware (higher sensitivity requires stronger evidence).
3. **Implement an assurance-gated onboarding workflow** in the access request/approval process:
   - Block access creation/entitlement until an **Assurance Record** exists and is current.
   - The Assurance Record must document which path is used: **Verified Controls** (with evidence) or **Approved Agreement** (with agreement metadata).
4. **Collect and review verification evidence** from the external host for the Verified Controls path. Accept only evidence that clearly covers the checklist items and is time-bounded (e.g., independent assessment reports, SOC 2/ISO-style reports, penetration test summaries where relevant, and signed attestations). Record reviewer identity, review date, coverage statement, and confidence rationale.
5. **For the Agreement path**, require an **approved, in-date, scope-matching** written agreement that explicitly covers the external system’s connection/processing of organisation-controlled information. Store the agreement as audit evidence and link it to the External System Register and Assurance Record.
6. **Enforce the gate technically** using your enterprise access management/conditional access (e.g., ZTNA/IdP conditional access, entitlement provisioning) so that external-system access is only possible when the Assurance Record status is “approved/current”. Ensure the enforcement applies to all relevant external-system activities (access, processing, storage, transmission) by tying entitlements to the external system identifier.
7. **Maintain audit-ready traceability**: for each external system and each access grant, retain the Assurance Record (verification evidence or approved agreement), the review/approval dates, and the mapping to information types/data flows.

## WHO (role responsible)
- **Information Security/Compliance Owner**: defines the assurance checklist and evidence acceptance criteria.
- **Third-Party Risk Management (TPRM) / Vendor Management**: manages evidence collection and agreement lifecycle.
- **IAM/Access Management Lead**: implements conditional access/entitlement enforcement.
- **System/Business Owner**: requests external system onboarding and provides data-flow/information-type context.

## Acceptance criteria
- No external-system entitlements are provisioned unless an Assurance Record exists and is current.
- For each external system, the Assurance Record clearly states whether it was approved via **Verified Controls** or **Approved Agreement**, and includes audit-ready evidence/metadata.
- Conditional access/entitlement enforcement prevents access when the Assurance Record is missing, expired, or not approved.
- Evidence/agreement coverage is traceable to the defined assurance checklist and linked to the external system register entry.
- Audit sampling confirms that access grants correlate to the correct external system Assurance Record and approval dates.

**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Create and populate an External System Register with data flows and information types for each external system
- [ ] Define an External System Assurance Checklist mapped to organisational security/privacy policies and plans, with risk-tier thresholds
- [ ] Implement an assurance-gated onboarding workflow in the access request/approval process that blocks entitlements without an approved Assurance Record
- [ ] Establish evidence collection and review procedures for the Verified Controls path, including time-bounded acceptance criteria and documented reviewer sign-off
- [ ] Create a contract/agreement repository workflow that enforces approved, in-date, scope-matching connection/processing agreements for the Agreement path
- [ ] Configure IAM/conditional access (e.g., ZTNA/IdP) to allow external-system access only when the linked Assurance Record status is approved/current
- [ ] Enable audit-ready traceability by linking each external-system access grant to the Assurance Record, evidence/agreement metadata, and approval dates

### ac-20.2 — Portable Storage Devices — Restricted Use (Enhancement)

> **Overview**
>
> This expectation is about keeping company USB sticks and other approved portable storage devices tightly controlled when they are plugged into other people’s or external computers, so they can’t be used to spread harmful software or move data where it shouldn’t go. Without these rules, a device could carry viruses or other malicious code into a new system, automatically start unwanted software the moment it’s connected, or allow copying of information onto unapproved removable media. To meet this expectation, the organisation must only permit authorised staff to use these devices for approved mission tasks, and only on external systems that have been given written permission for that use. The devices must be encrypted, scanned for threats immediately before and after each use, prevented from copying data to unmanaged removable media, and set so that auto-start behaviour is disabled when connected. The organisation should also keep clear written procedures, policies, and system settings records, with named responsibilities and agreements that define when and how these devices may be used.

#### Controlled encrypted USB workflow with scan-before/after and no auto-run

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT
Implement a controlled, auditable workflow for organisation-controlled portable storage devices (e.g., encrypted USB) so that authorised individuals may use them **only** for approved mission tasks on **external systems with written authorisation**, with technical safeguards including **encryption**, **malware scanning before and after use**, and **disabled auto-run**.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-20(2)** enhancement requires restricting the use of organisation-controlled portable storage devices by authorised individuals on external systems using the organisation-defined restrictions (**param: ac-20.02_odp / restrictions**). The organisation-defined restrictions include: use only for approved mission tasks; only on systems with written authorisation; no copying to unmanaged media; encrypt devices; scan before/after use; disable auto-run.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Standardise and harden devices (encryption + auto-run disabled):**
   - Issue only approved device models that are **hardware-encrypted** (or equivalent strong encryption) and have **auto-run/auto-play disabled** at device build/configuration time.
   - Maintain configuration evidence (device serial-to-policy mapping) in a central inventory.
2. **Enforce “written authorisation for external systems” via a check-out workflow:**
   - Create an ITSM/secure portal workflow that requires the user to select an **external system identifier** and an **approved mission task**.
   - The workflow must reference a **written authorisation record** (e.g., ticket/approval ID) before the device can be checked out.
3. **Scan-before-use gate (before connecting to the external system):**
   - Require the user to connect the device first to a hardened scanning station (or managed endpoint) that performs a malware scan and records results.
   - Only release the device for external-system use if the scan is clean; otherwise quarantine/block the device.
4. **Scan-after-use gate (immediately after disconnect):**
   - Require return to the scanning station immediately after the external-system session.
   - Perform a second malware scan and quarantine/block if any threats are detected.
5. **Prevent unmanaged copying in practice (workflow + external-system configuration):**
   - Configure the external systems (where feasible) to restrict removable media write/copy actions for the session (e.g., removable media controls / endpoint policy).
   - In the workflow, require the user to confirm “no copying to unmanaged media” and record the session outcome for auditability.

## WHO (role responsible)
- **Cybersecurity / IT Security Engineering:** define device standards, scanning requirements, and quarantine/block procedures.
- **IT Operations / Service Desk (ITSM owner):** implement and operate the check-out/check-in workflow and evidence capture.
- **System Owners of external systems:** provide and maintain the written authorisation records and apply removable-media restrictions for the authorised use cases.

## Acceptance criteria
- Only approved, encrypted devices with **auto-run disabled** are issued (verified via inventory/config evidence).
- Every external-system use has an associated **approved mission task** and **written authorisation reference** captured in the workflow.
- For each use session, there is recorded evidence of **malware scan before** connecting and **malware scan after** disconnecting.
- Devices are quarantined/blocked when scans fail.
- External-system configuration and/or session controls demonstrate enforcement of “no copying to unmanaged media” for the authorised use case (documented exceptions require approval).

**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Define approved portable device models and encryption/auto-run disable build standards and publish them to the device inventory team
- [ ] Implement an ITSM/secure portal workflow that captures user identity, approved mission task, external system identifier, and written authorisation reference before device check-out
- [ ] Deploy and harden a scanning station (or managed endpoint) to perform malware scans before connecting and record scan results with timestamps
- [ ] Configure devices so auto-run/auto-play is disabled and store device serial-to-policy evidence for audit
- [ ] Require mandatory device return to the scanning station after each external-system session and quarantine/block devices on failed scans
- [ ] Apply removable-media restrictions on authorised external systems for the session and document any approved exceptions

### ac-20.3 — Non-organizationally Owned Systems — Restricted Use (Enhancement)

> **Overview**
>
> This requirement is about stopping staff from using other people’s systems, or their own personal devices, to handle the organisation’s information unless it is done in a tightly controlled way. Without this, sensitive data could be exposed, lost, or accessed by the wrong people because external systems may not protect information to the same standard, and personal devices are harder to manage and investigate if something goes wrong. The organisation must clearly define what counts as a non-organisationally owned system or component, and only allow such systems to be used to process, store, or send organisational information after getting prior approval, with security protections the organisation has already reviewed and agreed, and with access limited to Confidential or Secret information only. Personally owned devices must not be used to process Classified information. The organisation must put these rules into written procedures and agreements, document how the systems are set up to enforce the limits, assign named responsibilities, and keep records showing who used what and when.

#### Approval-gated external/non-owned system access with data-class limits

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT
Implement an approval-gated mechanism that restricts use of **non-organisationally owned systems/components** (other organisations’ systems and personally owned devices) so they may only be used to **process, store, or transmit organisational information** under:
- **Prior approval** before authorisation
- **Organisation-approved security controls** being in place
- **Access limited to Confidential/Secret** information
- **Personally owned devices prohibited** from processing **Classified** information

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-20(3)** enhancement requires restricting non-organisationally owned systems/components to process, store, or transmit organisational information using the organisation-defined restrictions (**ac-20.03_odp: “Allowed only with prior approval, approved security controls, and access limited to Confidential/Secret data; personally owned devices prohibited for Classified processing.”**). The guidance also expects restrictions to be enforced via approved controls prior to authorising connection and to include legal/forensic considerations for personally owned devices.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define and operationalise “non-organisationally owned”
- Create a policy definition and workflow taxonomy covering:
  - Other organisations’ systems/components (e.g., vendor/partner SaaS, contractor-managed platforms, third-party cloud accounts not under your tenant)
  - Personally owned devices (BYOD) used for organisational access
- Require the intake to capture: system/component identity, owner, purpose, connection method, and requested data classification (Confidential/Secret/Classified).

### 2) Build a single approval workflow that gates authorisation
- Implement an ITSM/service request workflow that **must be approved before any connection/use is authorised**.
- Approval must include Information Security and the relevant system/network/application owner.
- The workflow must reject:
  - Any request that includes **Classified** data via non-organisationally owned systems/components.
  - Any request that uses **personally owned devices** for **Classified** processing.

### 3) Require evidence of “approved security controls” before approval
- In the workflow, require upload/attestation of security evidence aligned to your organisation’s approved control set (e.g., encryption in transit/at rest, strong authentication, least privilege, logging/monitoring, secure configuration baseline, vulnerability/patch posture where applicable).
- Store the approval record as audit evidence linking:
  - the external/non-owned system/component
  - the approved data classification limit (Confidential/Secret)
  - the approved security controls
  - the approvers and approval date

### 4) Enforce the classification limit technically at access time
- Bind the approval outcome to technical enforcement using your enterprise identity/access layer:
  - Use conditional access / access policies so access to the application and its data is only permitted for approved external integrations/users and only up to the approved classification scope.
  - For personally owned devices, enforce device-based restrictions (e.g., deny access for Classified scope; allow only for Confidential/Secret where permitted).
- Ensure enforcement is applied before access is granted (not after).

### 5) Add BYOD legal/forensic acknowledgement into the workflow
- For personally owned devices, require acceptance of terms covering incident response and forensic analysis expectations (as referenced in the AC-20 guidance to consult General Counsel for legal requirements).

## WHO (role responsible)
- **Information Security (or CISO delegate):** owns the approval criteria, approved security control set, and classification enforcement rules.
- **Application/System Owner:** validates that the external/non-owned system/component use case is legitimate and that the approved controls are applicable.
- **Service Desk/ITSM Process Owner:** implements the intake form and ensures requests cannot proceed without approval.
- **Identity & Access Management (IAM) Engineer:** implements conditional access/policy-as-code enforcement and device/classification gating.
- **Legal/General Counsel (as needed):** reviews BYOD terms for forensic/incident requirements.

## Acceptance criteria
- No external/non-organisationally owned system/component is authorised for organisational information processing/storing/transmission without a completed approval record.
- Requests involving **Classified** data are blocked for non-organisationally owned systems/components.
- **Personally owned devices** cannot be authorised for **Classified** processing; only Confidential/Secret access is permitted where allowed.
- Each approved authorisation has auditable evidence of the **approved security controls** and the **maximum permitted data classification**.
- Technical enforcement (conditional access / access policies) prevents access outside the approved classification scope.
- BYOD authorisations include documented legal/forensic acknowledgement terms.


**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Define in policy what constitutes a non-organisationally owned system/component and personally owned device for AC-20(3) scope
- [ ] Implement an ITSM intake and approval workflow that blocks authorisation until prior approval is recorded
- [ ] Create a required security-controls evidence checklist and link each approval to the approved controls and maximum data classification (Confidential/Secret only)
- [ ] Configure IAM conditional access/access policies to enforce the approved classification limit and deny access for unauthorised/non-approved external integrations and for BYOD Classified processing
- [ ] Add BYOD legal/forensic acknowledgement terms to the workflow and require acceptance before approval
- [ ] Establish audit logging and retention for approvals, access decisions, and enforcement outcomes to support compliance evidence

### ac-20.4 — Network Accessible Storage Devices — Prohibited Use (Enhancement)

> **Overview**
>
> This requirement is about stopping staff systems from using any shared storage that can be reached over a network from outside your organisation, including online storage provided through public, hybrid, or community cloud services. Without this, sensitive information could be copied, accessed, or exposed through external storage locations that are harder to control, increasing the risk of unauthorised access, data loss, or misuse by partners or third parties. To meet this expectation, the organisation must clearly state in its access rules and supporting procedures that all network-accessible storage devices (such as network-attached storage, storage networks, network file shares, and cloud object storage endpoints) are not permitted in external systems, and it must reflect this in system design, configuration settings, and the organisation’s security plan. It must keep a maintained list of the specific prohibited storage targets, ensure any external connection or processing agreements include the same ban, and retain audit records that show the prohibited storage was not used.

#### Enforce ban on network-accessible storage in external systems

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT
Prohibit the use of **all network-accessible storage devices** (NAS, SAN, SMB/NFS shares, and object storage endpoints) **in external systems**, including **online storage in public, hybrid, or community cloud-based systems**.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-20(4)** enhancement requires: **“Prohibit the use of {{ insert: param, ac-20.04_odp }} in external systems.”** The organisation-defined parameter **ac-20.04_odp** is **network-accessible storage devices** and the scope is **all such devices (NAS, SAN, SMB/NFS shares, object storage endpoints) in external systems**.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Define and publish the prohibition** in the organisation’s access control policy and supporting procedures, explicitly stating that **no network-accessible storage device** may be used in **external systems**, and that this includes **public/hybrid/community cloud online storage**.
2. **Create and maintain a prohibited storage registry** for the application and its environments, listing prohibited storage targets in a verifiable form (e.g., NAS/SAN hostnames, SMB/NFS share paths, object storage bucket/container identifiers, endpoint URLs), with an owner and change workflow.
3. **Implement technical enforcement** so prohibited storage cannot be used from the application environment:
   - Apply **egress/network controls** (firewall rules, proxy policies, DNS filtering) to block outbound connectivity from the application tiers to prohibited storage endpoints.
   - Apply **storage access controls** (IAM/ACLs) so service accounts and users cannot obtain permissions to mount/connect to external storage endpoints.
   - Where the application supports integrations (e.g., connectors for file/object storage), configure them to **allow only approved internal storage** and deny external storage endpoints by default.
4. **Ensure contractual/third-party alignment** by adding the prohibition to external connection/processing agreements (so partners cannot provide or request access to external network-accessible storage for this application).
5. **Generate audit evidence** by configuring logging and monitoring for storage-related actions (e.g., mount attempts, API calls to object storage endpoints, denied network attempts) and producing periodic reports that show **no successful use** of prohibited storage endpoints.

## WHO (role responsible)
- **Information Security Officer / Security Governance**: owns the policy/procedure update and prohibited storage registry governance.
- **Application Owner / Engineering Lead**: implements application integration restrictions and ensures service accounts cannot access prohibited endpoints.
- **Infrastructure/Network Team**: implements egress controls, DNS/proxy filtering, and network segmentation.
- **Procurement/Vendor Management**: ensures contractual clauses are included for external systems.
- **SIEM/Monitoring Team**: ensures audit logs are collected, retained, and reported.

## Acceptance criteria
- The organisation’s access control policy and procedures explicitly prohibit **all network-accessible storage devices** in **external systems**, including **public/hybrid/community cloud online storage**.
- A maintained prohibited storage registry exists and is current (with owner and update workflow).
- Technical controls prevent the application environment from establishing successful connections to any registry-listed prohibited storage endpoints (verified via test attempts and observed denied events).
- External/third-party agreements for relevant integrations include the same prohibition.
- Audit evidence (logs and periodic reports) demonstrates that **no successful access/mount/integration** to prohibited external storage occurred during the reporting period.

**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Update access control policy and procedures to explicitly prohibit all network-accessible storage devices in external systems, including public/hybrid/community cloud online storage
- [ ] Create and maintain a prohibited storage registry (NAS/SAN hostnames, SMB/NFS share paths, object storage bucket/container identifiers, endpoint URLs) with an owner and change workflow
- [ ] Implement egress/network controls (firewall/proxy/DNS filtering) to block outbound connectivity from application tiers to registry-listed prohibited storage endpoints
- [ ] Restrict storage permissions for application users and service accounts (IAM/ACLs) so no identities can mount/connect to external storage endpoints
- [ ] Configure application storage integrations/connectors to allow only approved internal storage and deny external storage endpoints by default
- [ ] Add the storage prohibition clause to external connection/processing agreements for any third-party/vendor integrations involving storage
- [ ] Enable and retain audit logging for storage access attempts and denied events, and produce periodic evidence reports showing no successful use of prohibited endpoints

### ac-20.5 — Portable Storage Devices — Prohibited Use (Enhancement)

> **Overview**
>
> This requirement is essentially a strict rule that staff must not plug the organisation’s own USB drives or other organisation-managed portable storage into systems that the organisation does not directly control. The real-world risk is that these devices can carry malware or copy sensitive information onto partner, customer, contractor, or other external environments, sometimes without anyone noticing until damage is done. To meet this expectation, the organisation must clearly define what counts as an external system and publish a complete ban in its access rules and supporting procedures, so staff know what is and is not allowed. It must also enforce the ban in practice, using a mix of system settings that block portable storage where feasible and documented processes such as training and approvals for any needed data movement. Responsibility must be assigned to named roles, including system and network administrators and information security staff, and the organisation must reflect the ban in system design and security planning, include it in connection or processing agreements, and keep audit records showing the rule is being applied.

#### Deny organisation USB storage on external systems with audit evidence

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT
Prohibit authorised users from using organisation-controlled portable storage devices (e.g., USB mass storage) on any external systems by enforcing a complete ban through technical controls where feasible and process controls where technical enforcement is incomplete.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST AC-20(5) (enhancement) requires a **complete prohibition** of organisation-controlled portable storage devices by authorised individuals on **external systems**, with enforcement using **technical methods and/or nontechnical (process-based) methods**.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Define scope of “external system”** in the access control policy and supporting procedure(s): any system not directly owned/managed by the organisation (e.g., partner/customer/contractor environments, third-party managed systems, internet-accessible customer VMs, unmanaged guest workstations, and any system outside approved enterprise management boundaries).
2. **Implement technical enforcement on endpoints used to access external systems**:
   - Apply an endpoint baseline that **denies USB mass storage/removable media** by default (OS/device-control settings managed centrally).
   - Use conditional enforcement so the deny applies when the endpoint is in an “external access” context (e.g., connecting via partner network/VPN profile, using a browser session to an external domain category, or when the endpoint is assigned to an “external access” device group).
   - Where organisation-controlled portable devices must exist, enforce an **allow-list for approved transfer mechanisms** (e.g., managed secure transfer tooling) and ensure the portable-media path is blocked for external access contexts.
3. **Implement process-based enforcement** for any unavoidable exceptions:
   - Require a documented, pre-approved exception workflow (Information Security + system/data owner approval) that specifies the approved transfer method and compensating controls.
   - Provide staff guidance on approved alternatives (e.g., encrypted file transfer, approved collaboration channels, or managed secure transfer devices) and explicitly state that organisation-controlled USB devices must not be plugged into external systems.
4. **Ensure auditability and evidence generation**:
   - Enable logging for removable media connection attempts and block/deny outcomes, including user identity, device identifier, timestamp, and target system context.
   - Forward logs to the SIEM and retain per the organisation’s log retention standard.
   - Produce periodic compliance reports showing the deny rule is active and that blocks are occurring (and that exceptions are tracked).
5. **Assign named responsibilities**:
   - Endpoint management administrators own the technical deny configuration.
   - Information Security owns the policy/procedure and exception governance.
   - Application/system owners ensure the “external access” contexts are correctly mapped to the enforcement groups.

## WHO (role responsible)
- **Information Security Officer / Security Governance**: owns the AC-20(5) policy/procedure, defines “external system”, runs exception governance.
- **Endpoint Management Administrator (IT)**: implements and maintains the USB/removable media deny configuration and logging.
- **Application/System Owner**: ensures external access contexts are correctly identified and mapped to enforcement groups.
- **SIEM/Monitoring Team**: ensures logs are collected, normalised, and retained for audit.

## Acceptance criteria
- The organisation has a published procedure defining “external system” and stating a **complete prohibition** on using organisation-controlled portable storage devices on external systems.
- Endpoints that can access external systems have a centrally managed configuration that **denies USB mass storage/removable media** by default, with enforcement active in external-access contexts.
- All removable-media connection attempts on affected endpoints generate logs showing **block/deny** outcomes (or approved exception handling), and logs are available in SIEM for audit.
- Any exception requires documented pre-approval with compensating controls, and exception records are retained.
- A compliance report can be produced demonstrating the deny rule is active and exceptions (if any) are controlled.

**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Define and publish the term “external system” in the access control policy and supporting procedure(s)
- [ ] Configure centrally managed endpoint device-control to deny USB mass storage/removable media by default
- [ ] Implement conditional enforcement so the deny applies specifically during external-access contexts (e.g., external VPN profile/device group)
- [ ] Create an exception workflow requiring pre-approval and compensating controls for any permitted data movement involving external systems
- [ ] Enable and forward logs for removable-media connection attempts and block/deny outcomes to the SIEM with user and device identifiers
- [ ] Run a compliance check and produce an audit-ready report demonstrating the deny rule is active and exceptions are tracked

### ac-21 — Information Sharing (Control)

> **Overview**
>
> This expectation is about making sure people only share sensitive information with the right partners, for the right reasons, and under the right legal and access conditions. Without it, an organisation could accidentally disclose classified or contract-sensitive material to someone who is not properly authorised, or share it without the required agreements, leading to serious legal, financial, and reputational harm. To meet this requirement, the organisation must give authorised staff a way to check that the access granted to a sharing partner matches the specific restrictions attached to the information, including any special access programme or compartment rules and any non-disclosure agreement requirements. It must also provide clear, policy-based guidance that uses the information’s sensitivity labels, performs automated eligibility checks, and prompts the user to confirm the required agreement and special access conditions before proceeding. Where automation is not enough, the organisation must define when staff must use judgement and record the decision and rationale.

#### Policy-based sharing workflow with access-match and NDA/SAP checks

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT must be done
Implement an information-sharing workflow that assists authorised users in deciding whether a sharing partner’s access authorisations match the information’s required access and use restrictions, including any NDA-governed requirements and any special access programme/compartment (SAP/compartment) restrictions. The workflow must use policy-based guidance driven by information classification tags and must include automated access checks and mandatory validations (with user discretion only in defined circumstances).

## WHY (control requirement)
AC-21 requires that information sharing accounts for restricted information determined by formal/administrative determinations, and that sharing decisions verify that the sharing partner’s authorisations match the information’s access/use restrictions. The guidance further expects automated mechanisms (or manual processes) to assist users in making sharing/collaboration decisions, including use of security attributes and information flow techniques.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Define machine-readable sharing restrictions**: Create a mapping from your enterprise data classification tags to required access/use restrictions, including: allowed actions (e.g., view/edit/download), required partner eligibility types, and required validation attributes (NDA required? SAP/compartment ID required?).
2. **Bind each shareable item to restrictions**: Ensure the application (or its metadata ingestion/classification integration) stores classification tags and required restriction attributes alongside the content/record so the workflow can derive the “information’s required restrictions” (not the partner’s general access level).
3. **Create/maintain a partner eligibility and authorisation source**: Maintain a partner directory (individual/group/organisation) that records whether the partner has an approved NDA and which SAP/compartment authorisations they hold. Integrate with IAM/entitlement systems and NDA/SAP/contract repositories.
4. **Implement the sharing request workflow**: Add a “request/approve sharing” step (portal, ticketing integration, or in-app action) that captures: information item identifier, intended access type, sharing partner, and purpose. The workflow must run an **automated access-match check** comparing:
   - (a) the information’s required restrictions derived from tags/attributes, and
   - (b) the sharing partner’s authorisations/eligibility for NDA and SAP/compartment.
5. **Enforce mandatory validations and prompts**: If the information is tagged as NDA-governed and/or SAP/compartment-governed, the workflow must require the user to confirm the correct NDA/SAP/compartment authorisation context and must block completion until the automated checks indicate eligibility.
6. **Support defined user discretion with auditability**: Where discretion is permitted (per your organisation-defined circumstances), require the user to select a discretion reason, provide a rationale, and record the decision outcome. Ensure the workflow logs the automated-check results, prompt completion status, and the final decision.
7. **Generate audit-ready evidence**: Persist workflow configuration (rules/policy-as-code), decision logs, and the authoritative mapping of tags→restrictions, plus references to NDA/SAP/compartment validation records used during the decision.

## WHO (role responsible)
- **Application Owner / Product Owner**: ensures the workflow is implemented in the application and that sharing actions route through it.
- **Information Security / Data Governance Lead**: defines the classification-tag-to-restriction mapping and the discretion circumstances.
- **IAM/Identity Engineer**: integrates partner eligibility/authorisations and ensures automated access-match checks are accurate.
- **Legal/Contracts (NDA/SAP governance)**: maintains authoritative NDA and SAP/compartment eligibility records consumed by the workflow.
- **Security Assurance / Compliance**: validates audit evidence and test results.

## Acceptance criteria
- For NDA-governed and/or SAP/compartment-governed information, sharing cannot be completed unless automated access-match checks confirm the partner’s eligibility and the user completes mandatory NDA/SAP/compartment prompts.
- The workflow derives required restrictions from the information’s classification tags/attributes and compares them to the partner’s authorisations/eligibility (no reliance on partner general access level alone).
- All sharing decisions produce an auditable record including: information item ID, partner ID, intended access type, automated-check results, prompt completion status, and (where discretion is used) user rationale.
- Evidence exists for: the tag→restriction mapping, workflow configuration/rules, and integration points to NDA/SAP/compartment and IAM/entitlement sources.

**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Define and publish a machine-readable mapping from data classification tags to required access/use restrictions, including NDA and SAP/compartment attributes
- [ ] Modify the application/integration to store classification tags and required restriction attributes with each shareable information item
- [ ] Integrate the sharing workflow with IAM/entitlement and NDA/SAP/compartment eligibility sources to obtain partner authorisations
- [ ] Implement an automated access-match check that compares information-required restrictions to partner eligibility for the requested access type
- [ ] Configure mandatory prompts and hard blocks for NDA-governed and SAP/compartment-governed sharing until automated eligibility is confirmed
- [ ] Implement audit logging for every sharing decision, including automated-check results, prompt completion status, and user rationale when discretion is used
- [ ] Create test cases and run validation to prove blocked/allowed outcomes for NDA/SAP/compartment scenarios and defined discretion circumstances

### ac-21.1 — Automated Decision Support (Enhancement)

> **Overview**
>
> This requirement is about making sure information is shared only when the right people ask for it and the system checks, automatically and consistently, that the receiving partner is allowed to get that specific information. Without this, staff could accidentally (or improperly) share sensitive material with the wrong organisation, or share more than they should, creating legal, financial, and reputational harm. To meet this expectation, the organisation must set up policy-based workflow and approval gates so that sharing decisions can be triggered only by users who are authorised to make those decisions, and every request is automatically checked against two things: the partner’s current permission to receive information, and the specific access restrictions attached to the information being shared. The organisation must keep up-to-date records of who can make decisions, which partners are allowed, and what restrictions apply, configure the system to enforce these rules without manual bypass, and document how the automated checks work so evidence is available that the system’s decisions were based on the current, correct information.

#### Automated policy-gated sharing decisions by authorised users

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT
Implement automated decision support that enforces information-sharing decisions by authorised users, based on:
1) the sharing partner’s current access authorisations, and
2) access restrictions attached to the specific information being shared.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 AC-21(1) enhancement requires that automated mechanisms are used to enforce information-sharing decisions by authorised users, using the organisation-defined parameter **ac-21.01_odp (“automated mechanisms”)**. The decision must be based on partner authorisations and information-specific access restrictions.

## HOW (specific approach)
1. **Create authoritative policy inputs (system-generated data):**
   - Maintain a machine-readable catalogue of **information access restrictions** (e.g., by data classification, dataset/object type, sensitivity labels, and required constraints such as allowed recipient categories, required approvals, and time limits).
   - Maintain a machine-readable catalogue of **sharing partners** and their **access authorisations** (e.g., external tenant/vendor/service principal entitlements, allowed information categories, and any contractual constraints).
   - Maintain a machine-readable list of **users authorised to make sharing decisions** (decision-maker/approver roles), sourced from the enterprise IdP/authorisation system.
2. **Implement an automated workflow/approval gate:**
   - Treat “share” as an access-grant request that cannot activate until policy evaluation completes.
   - Integrate the application’s sharing endpoints (UI/API/background jobs) with a workflow engine or policy decision point so that every share request triggers automated evaluation of:
     - **Partner authorisation** for the requested partner identity and requested information category/object.
     - **Information access restrictions** for the specific information asset/object (including any required approvals/constraints).
   - Enforce that only users in the **authorised decision-maker** role can submit/approve the request; all other users can only request.
3. **Prevent bypass and enforce activation controls:**
   - Remove/disable direct “grant sharing” paths for non-decision-makers.
   - Ensure any API calls, background processes, or admin actions that would effect sharing must call the same policy-gated decision mechanism (no alternate code paths).
4. **Generate auditable decision records:**
   - For each share request, record a system-generated decision log containing: requester identity, decision-maker identity (if applicable), partner identity, information asset/object identifier, policy version, evaluated partner authorisations, evaluated information restrictions, decision outcome (allow/deny), and timestamp.
   - Forward decision logs to the enterprise SIEM/logging platform for retention and auditability.
5. **Operationalise policy-as-code and change control:**
   - Store policy rules and mappings in version-controlled configuration (policy-as-code) with change management.
   - Ensure the workflow uses the latest approved policy version and that evidence can be produced showing which rules were evaluated.

## WHO (roles responsible)
- **Application Owner / Product Security Lead:** accountable for implementing the policy-gated sharing workflow and ensuring enforcement is complete.
- **Identity & Access Management (IAM) Lead:** provides/maintains decision-maker roles and partner identity mappings.
- **Data Governance Lead:** defines and maintains information access restrictions taxonomy and mappings.
- **Security Engineering / Platform Team:** implements policy decision integration, bypass prevention, and audit logging.
- **Compliance/Audit Liaison:** validates evidence generation and test results.

## Acceptance criteria
- Every information-sharing action that results in access being granted is preceded by automated policy evaluation using both partner authorisations and information access restrictions.
- Only users in the authorised decision-maker role can approve/activate sharing outcomes; non-authorised users cannot bypass the workflow.
- For each share request, the system produces an auditable decision record showing the evaluated partner authorisations, evaluated information restrictions, policy version, and allow/deny outcome.
- The enforcement applies consistently across UI, API, and any automated/background sharing mechanisms (no alternate bypass paths).

**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Define a machine-readable information access restriction model mapped to shareable assets/objects
- [ ] Define a machine-readable sharing partner authorisation model mapped to partner identities and allowed information categories
- [ ] Configure the enterprise IdP/authorisation system with a dedicated decision-maker role and ensure only that role can approve/activate sharing
- [ ] Implement a policy-gated sharing workflow so every share request triggers automated evaluation of partner authorisations and information restrictions before activation
- [ ] Remove or refactor all direct sharing/grant code paths so they call the same policy decision mechanism (no bypass via UI/API/background jobs)
- [ ] Implement system-generated decision records capturing evaluated inputs, policy version, and allow/deny outcome; forward to SIEM for audit retention
- [ ] Validate enforcement with end-to-end tests covering allow/deny outcomes, unauthorised bypass attempts, and policy version correctness

### ac-21.2 — Information Search and Retrieval (Enhancement)

> **Overview**
>
> This requirement is about making sure that when people search for documents or information, they only see what they are officially allowed to see, and only in the approved situations for sensitive material. Without this, someone could accidentally or deliberately discover restricted Secret or Confidential content, or share it with the wrong customer, partner, country, or programme, creating serious legal and contractual exposure, including export-control and compliance breaches. To meet this expectation, the organisation must clearly define who can receive Secret and Confidential information and the approved sharing boundaries for it, and then build and configure its search service so it filters results based on the user’s permission and the item’s sharing rules. It must also follow the applicable export-control and compliance requirements for Secret and Confidential data, keep documented procedures and design information showing how these restrictions work, and retain records of searches and the enforcement decisions so the organisation can review and prove what was shown or blocked.

#### ABAC policy-as-code to filter Secret/Confidential search results

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT
Implement information search and retrieval services that enforce the organisation’s **information-sharing restrictions** (AC-21.02_odp) by filtering search results at query-time based on **(1) the user’s authorisation** and **(2) the approved data-sharing boundaries** for Secret/Confidential information, including enforcement of **ITAR/EAR** and **CMMC-L2/L3** constraints.

## WHY (control requirement)
AC-21(2) (Enhancement) requires: **“Implement information search and retrieval services that enforce {{ insert: param, ac-21.02_odp }}.”** The guidance further requires that search services **identify information system resources relevant to an information need** while ensuring only permitted resources are returned.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Create an authoritative metadata model** for all Secret/Confidential content indexed by the search service, including: classification level, ITAR/EAR tags, required CMMC level (L2/L3), and sharing-boundary attributes (e.g., programme/customer/partner/country).
2. **Define user/recipient authorisation attributes** in the identity/access layer (e.g., clearance/authorisation, approved programmes, permitted countries, partner account mapping, and CMMC status where applicable for external recipients).
3. **Implement ABAC policy-as-code** in the search service enforcement path (policy decision point + enforcement point). Policies must evaluate both user attributes and item attributes and return an enforcement decision (allow/withhold) with a **reason code** (e.g., boundary mismatch, ITAR/EAR not permitted, CMMC level not satisfied).
4. **Compile policies into a system-held restriction list** (derived from the authoritative metadata and policy-as-code) that the search service uses to filter results **before** they are returned to the user.
5. **Enforce inheritance for downstream actions**: ensure that any “open/download/export/share” actions originating from search results re-check the same ABAC decision (so filtered-out items cannot be retrieved via follow-on endpoints).
6. **Make enforcement auditable**: log each search query and the enforcement outcomes (which item identifiers were returned vs withheld, and the reason code) and forward to SIEM for review and anomaly detection (e.g., repeated boundary probing).
7. **Operationalise change control**: version policies and restriction-list compilation; require approval for policy changes affecting Secret/Confidential sharing boundaries.

## WHO (role responsible)
- **Application owner / solution architect**: owns the design and integration of the ABAC enforcement into the search service.
- **IAM engineer**: defines and maintains user/recipient attributes and mappings.
- **Data governance / compliance lead**: defines approved sharing boundaries and ITAR/EAR/CMMC enforcement requirements.
- **Security engineering**: ensures logging, auditability, and SIEM integration.

## Acceptance criteria
- For Secret/Confidential indexed content, search results are returned **only** when the user is authorised **and** the request falls within the approved sharing boundaries defined for AC-21.02_odp.
- Items are withheld with a recorded **reason code** when boundary/ITAR-EAR/CMMC-L2-L3 constraints are not satisfied.
- Downstream actions (open/download/export/share) from search results cannot bypass the ABAC decision.
- Search enforcement decisions (allow/withhold) are logged with sufficient detail for audit review and are available in SIEM.
- Policy changes are versioned and governed through the organisation’s change control process.

**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Define and document approved Secret/Confidential sharing boundaries (programme/customer/partner/country) and map them to item metadata attributes
- [ ] Model Secret/Confidential indexable content with classification, ITAR/EAR tags, and required CMMC-L2/L3 attributes
- [ ] Create user/recipient authorisation attributes in IAM (clearance/authorisation, permitted programmes, permitted countries, partner mappings, CMMC status where applicable)
- [ ] Implement ABAC policy-as-code integrated into the search service to decide allow/withhold per item using user and item attributes
- [ ] Generate and deploy a system-held restriction list used by the search service to filter results at query-time
- [ ] Enforce the same ABAC decision on downstream retrieval actions (open/download/export/share) originating from search results
- [ ] Enable audit logging of search queries and enforcement outcomes (returned vs withheld item identifiers with reason codes) and forward to SIEM

### ac-22 — Publicly Accessible Content (Control)

> **Overview**
>
> This requirement is about preventing private or confidential information from accidentally ending up on your organisation’s public website or other public-facing pages. Without it, staff could publish sensitive material such as private personal details, internal documents, confidential contract information, or proprietary information, which could cause legal trouble, reputational damage, and harm to customers or employees. To meet this expectation, the organisation must appoint specific people who are allowed to publish public content, train them so they clearly understand they must not include any non-public information, and put a process in place to review every proposed item before it is posted to confirm it contains nothing that should stay private. After content is live, the organisation must check the public-facing content every day and promptly remove anything non-public that is discovered, keeping records of these checks and actions.

#### Authorised public content publishing workflow with daily review

- **Category:** Manual
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT
Implement a controlled publishing workflow for all publicly accessible content so that only specifically authorised and trained individuals can publish, every item is reviewed before it becomes public, and public pages are reviewed daily to detect and promptly remove any non-public information.

## WHY (control requirement)
AC-22 requires management of individuals who make information publicly accessible and aims to prevent the public from gaining access to non-public information (including protected and proprietary information). The organisation-defined parameter **ac-22_odp (frequency)** sets the required review frequency for publicly accessible content.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Define scope of “publicly accessible systems”** (e.g., public website CMS, public landing pages, public downloads, public knowledge base, public-facing portals) and ensure the workflow applies to all production publishing paths.
2. **Maintain an authorised publisher list** as the source of truth (named individuals/roles) and map it to CMS/web platform permissions (no shared accounts). Track each publisher’s training/authorisation status.
3. **Enforce technical publishing gates (RBAC/workflow)**: publishers may submit drafts; only designated reviewers/approvers can publish to production. Require identity-based access via the enterprise IdP (with MFA) and remove access when authorisation expires.
4. **Implement a pre-publication review checklist** that must be completed and evidenced before publishing (e.g., confirm no personal data, internal-only documents, confidential contract terms, credentials/secrets, security architecture details, incident details, or proprietary information).
5. **Record approval evidence**: every publish action must reference a pre-publication approval record (ticket/checklist/sign-off) created before the publish timestamp.
6. **Perform daily review at the required frequency** (**ac-22_odp default: daily**) of the public-facing content using a repeatable checklist (focus on “latest”/news/updates, downloads, and any frequently edited pages). Capture evidence in a ticketing/GRC log.
7. **Prompt removal and remediation logging**: when non-public information is found, immediately remove/rollback to the last known-good version, then record what was removed, when, by whom, and the remediation outcome.

## WHO (role responsible)
- **Public Content Owner / Web Governance Lead**: owns scope, authorised publisher list, and the daily review process.
- **CMS/Web Platform Administrator**: implements RBAC/workflow gates and integrates with the enterprise IdP.
- **Authorised Publishers**: complete the pre-publication checklist and submit drafts.
- **Approvers/Reviewers**: validate checklist outcomes and approve publishing.
- **Security/Compliance (GRC)**: audits evidence (authorised list, approvals, daily review logs) and tracks remediation.

## Acceptance criteria
- Only individuals on the authorised publisher list can submit content for publication, and only approvers can publish to production.
- Every production publish has a recorded pre-publication approval/checklist reference created before the publish timestamp.
- Daily review evidence exists for all in-scope public pages for the last review period (at least daily per **ac-22_odp**), including checklist results.
- A tested removal/rollback procedure exists and is used with documented evidence when non-public information is discovered.
- CMS permissions are periodically validated against the authorised publisher list (at least when authorisation changes).

**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Define and document the in-scope publicly accessible systems and publishing paths for AC-22 coverage
- [ ] Create and maintain an authorised publisher list and map it to CMS/web platform RBAC roles (no shared accounts)
- [ ] Implement a pre-publication workflow gate requiring checklist completion and approver sign-off before production publish
- [ ] Integrate publishing access with the enterprise IdP and enforce MFA for publishers and approvers
- [ ] Establish a daily review procedure (per ac-22_odp) with a repeatable checklist and ticket/GRC evidence capture
- [ ] Create a removal/rollback playbook and ensure remediation records capture what/when/who and the outcome
- [ ] Run a periodic permission validation to detect drift between the authorised publisher list and actual CMS permissions

### ac-23 — Data Mining Protection (Control)

> **Overview**
>
> This requirement is about stopping people from repeatedly poking at sensitive databases to slowly work out confidential details, even if they are allowed to ask questions in the first place. Without these protections, someone could automate many queries to extract patterns or exact information, potentially exposing personal data or other highly sensitive secrets, including through insider misuse. To meet this expectation, the organisation must first clearly identify which database records and specific fields are classed as Confidential or Secret, and define and document what kinds of data analysis are genuinely authorised, including a process to check authorisation before any data mining happens. It must then limit how often and how many queries can be run against that sensitive data, allow only the minimum access needed for each authorised task, and block or restrict requests that go beyond the permitted scope. It must also watch for unusual query behaviour, alert the right people for investigation, keep audit records for review, and, where feasible, use privacy-preserving output methods so repeated querying is harder to exploit.

#### Protected-data query gateway with throttling, scope limits, alerts

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT
Implement a central query control plane (gateway/service layer) that all application access to **protected data storage objects** must use. The gateway enforces **rate limiting and query throttling**, **least-privilege query controls** (including scope/field/row restrictions), **detection and alerting for atypical mining-like query behaviour**, and (where feasible) routes analytics to **differential-privacy-enabled** query mechanisms.

## WHY (control requirement)
AC-23 requires the organisation to employ the specified **data mining prevention and detection techniques** for the specified **data storage objects** to detect and protect against unauthorised data mining. The control guidance explicitly calls out limiting query frequency/number, limiting response types, applying differential privacy where feasible, and notifying personnel when atypical database queries/access occur.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Define protected objects**: Create an authoritative mapping of database **records and fields** that contain **Confidential and Secret** data (e.g., table/column/row filters) and register them in a protected-data catalogue.
2. **Define authorised mining rules**: Implement policy-as-code that specifies which query patterns/templates are permitted for each protected object (e.g., allowed predicates, allowed aggregations, maximum result cardinality, required join paths, and disallowed high-cardinality extraction patterns).
3. **Enforce least-privilege at query time**: Route all protected-data queries through the gateway. The gateway must deny or rewrite queries that attempt to broaden scope (e.g., requesting unauthorised columns, removing required predicates, expanding row sets, or using query shapes associated with extraction).
4. **Apply rate limiting and throttling**: Configure per-identity and per-protected-object limits (queries per minute/hour and result-row/minute caps). Use separate thresholds for interactive users versus service accounts and batch jobs.
5. **Detect atypical mining-like behaviour**: Emit structured telemetry for each allowed/denied/throttled query (identity, query template/hash/shape, targeted protected objects, estimated/returned cardinality, frequency). Feed this into the SIEM and generate alerts on deviations from baselines (e.g., sudden increases in query rate, repeated access to many distinct protected fields, or unusual query shapes).
6. **Differential privacy where feasible**: For analytics/reporting use-cases that require repeated querying of protected fields, route requests to DP-enabled stored procedures/templates or DP-wrapped endpoints. Ensure the gateway blocks direct “raw” result paths for protected fields when DP is required.
7. **Maintain audit evidence and response procedure**: Log all enforcement decisions (allow/deny/throttle), policy versions, and alert outcomes. Define an operational runbook for investigation and escalation when alerts indicate unauthorised mining.

## WHO
- **Data Protection Officer / Privacy & Legal Counsel**: confirm authorisation requirements and privacy constraints for any permitted mining and DP feasibility.
- **Application Owner / Data Platform Owner**: approve protected-data catalogue and authorised query templates.
- **Security Engineering (SIEM/SOAR integration)**: implement telemetry, alert rules, and escalation workflows.
- **Database/Platform Engineers**: implement the query gateway/service layer, policy-as-code, and DP-enabled query templates.

## Acceptance criteria
- All application/service access paths to the identified **Confidential/Secret** database **records and fields** are mediated by the query gateway (no bypass paths).
- The gateway enforces **rate limiting/query throttling** and **least-privilege query controls** such that unauthorised scope expansion is denied or rewritten.
- The system generates and forwards alerts for **atypical query behaviour** (e.g., abnormal frequency, unusual query shapes, or broad protected-field targeting) to the SIEM with sufficient context for investigation.
- For supported analytics use-cases, outputs are produced via **differential privacy mechanisms** (or documented rationale for why DP is not feasible for specific cases, with compensating controls).
- Audit logs exist showing enforcement decisions, policy versioning, and alert handling outcomes for a representative set of test cases (allowed, denied, throttled, and alerted).

**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Create and approve a protected-data catalogue mapping Confidential/Secret database records and fields to gateway policy targets
- [ ] Implement policy-as-code for authorised query templates/patterns per protected object, including required predicates and disallowed extraction shapes
- [ ] Deploy a query gateway/service layer that mediates all access to protected objects and denies or rewrites unauthorised scope (fields/rows/predicates)
- [ ] Configure per-identity and per-protected-object rate limiting and query throttling thresholds, including result-row caps
- [ ] Integrate query telemetry with the SIEM and implement alert rules for atypical mining-like query behaviour
- [ ] Implement differential-privacy-enabled query templates/endpoints for feasible analytics use-cases and block raw protected-field outputs where required
- [ ] Establish an investigation runbook and retain audit logs of allow/deny/throttle decisions with policy version evidence

### ac-24 — Access Control Decisions (Control)

> **Overview**
>
> This requirement is about making sure every time someone tries to use a system or access a resource, the organisation’s permission decision is worked out first and only then is access allowed or blocked. Without this, there is a risk that people could get in when they should not, or that sensitive actions could happen before the organisation has properly checked whether they are authorised, leading to data loss, fraud, or disruption. To meet this expectation, the organisation must write clear, documented procedures that explain how authorisation decisions are made for every access attempt, and how those decisions are applied before any access is enforced. It must also ensure the system is set up so that this decision-before-access sequence happens for all relevant types of access, including logins, files or shared folders, applications, and administrative actions. Finally, it must keep audit records showing the decision outcome for each access request so the organisation can prove what happened.

#### Decision-before-enforcement via PDP/PEP for every access request

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical

## WHAT must be done
Implement an authorisation decision step for **every** access request, and ensure that the system **applies the access control decision before enforcing access** (i.e., before any content is served, business logic is executed, or privileged/admin actions complete).

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-24** requires that **{{ insert: param, ac-24_odp.01 }}** are applied to each access request **prior to access enforcement**, where **{{ insert: param, ac-24_odp.02 }}** are defined as the access control decisions.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Define and document the decision workflow** for the application: for each request, specify the inputs to the authorisation decision (subject identity/claims, resource identifier, action, environment/context), the policy evaluation process, and the decision output (allow/deny plus decision rationale/obligations).
2. **Implement a Policy Decision Point (PDP)** (e.g., policy engine service) that evaluates the authorisation model and returns an explicit decision for each request.
3. **Implement a Policy Enforcement Point (PEP)** at every enforcement choke point in the application path(s): API gateway, service middleware, application controllers, and any administrative endpoints. Configure the PEP so that it **blocks by default** and **requires a PDP decision** before proceeding.
4. **Enforce the decision-before-enforcement sequence in code/config**: the PEP must not return success, execute protected business logic, or access protected data until the PDP decision is received. If the PDP is unavailable, default to **deny** (or a documented compensating mechanism consistent with organisational policy).
5. **Ensure decision coverage across all access types**: web UI actions, API calls, background/async jobs that act on behalf of users, file/resource downloads, and administrative functions (including “impersonation” or privileged operations).
6. **Generate audit evidence per request**: log a correlation identifier for each access request and record the PDP decision outcome (allow/deny), the evaluated subject/resource/action, and the enforcement result. Ensure logs are centralised to the SIEM/monitoring platform.
7. **Test the sequence**: add automated integration tests that assert the PDP decision is produced and recorded **before** enforcement occurs (e.g., verify that protected handlers are not invoked when PDP returns deny).

## WHO (role responsible)
- **Application Security Engineer / Solution Architect**: defines the authorisation model and decision workflow.
- **Backend/Platform Engineers**: implement PDP/PEP integration and enforcement sequencing.
- **Security Operations / SOC**: validates audit logging, correlation, and alerting for deny decisions.
- **Change Manager / Release Manager**: ensures controlled rollout via standard change management.

## Acceptance criteria
- For every protected access path (user, service account, admin), the system obtains an explicit **allow/deny** decision from the PDP **before** any enforcement action occurs.
- Automated tests demonstrate that when PDP returns **deny**, protected business logic/data access is not executed and the request is blocked.
- Audit logs for each request include a correlation ID and record the PDP decision outcome and enforcement outcome.
- Administrative endpoints and non-interactive actions (e.g., async jobs) are covered by the same decision-before-enforcement mechanism.

**Actions Required for Compliance:**

- [ ] Document the per-request authorisation decision workflow (inputs, evaluation, allow/deny output, obligations) for the application
- [ ] Deploy/configure a PDP that returns an explicit allow/deny decision for each request based on the defined authorisation model
- [ ] Place a PEP at every enforcement choke point (API gateway, application middleware/controllers, admin endpoints) and configure block-by-default
- [ ] Modify protected request handling so enforcement (serving data/executing logic) occurs only after the PDP decision is received
